# [Medicalstudyzone.com] Rafi Golden 14 Medicine Feb plus May 22.pdf (Cleaned)

## Page 1

1. When ejection fraction increases, there will be a decrease in:
   a. End diastolic volume
   b. End systolic volume
   c. Cardiac index
   d. Cardiac output
   e. Pulse pressure
   **Ans: B**

Autosomal dominant is different from autosomal recessive:
   a. Only male carrier
   b. Complete penetrance is common
   c. Heterozygous is affected
   d. Only female affected.
   **Ans: C**

A patient with anaphylactic shock compared to hypovolemic shock most likely has one of the followings:
   a. Cardiac output is higher than normal
   b. Heart rate is greater than normal
   c. Serum creatinine is elevated
   d. Total peripheral resistance is greater than normal
   e. Ventricular contractility is greater than normal
   **Ans: A**

Which of the following is the cause of increase pulse pressure?
   a. Increase Stroke volume
   b. Decrease venous compliance
   c. Increase Venous compliance and cardiac output
   d. Increase total peripheral resistance
   e. Increase heart rate with constant
   **Ans: A**

In a patient, damage to the nerve arising from the dorsal brainstem will likely cause?
   a. Ptosis of the left eye
   b. Loss of intorsion
   c. Mydriasis
   d. Cycloplegia
   e. Loss of extrusion
   **Ans: B**

A 50- year- old female with diabetes for 20 years, complains of abdominal distension after meals due to diabetic gastroparesis. Which of the following is most suitable drug for relief of her symptoms?
   a. Antacids
   b. Loperamide
   c. Metoclopramide
   d. Omeprazole
   e. Sucralfate
   **Ans: C**

A 30- years lady presented in eye OPs with history of fever, headache and diplopia. O/E it was found that she is having ptosis. Mydriasis, microcoria and crossed horizontal diplopia. The most likely diagnosis is?
   a. Head injury
   b. Oculomotor nerve damage
   c. Horner's syndrome
   d. Hypotroldism
   e. Tochear nerve damage.
   **Ans: B** (Ptosis + dilated pupil = third nerve palsy; Ptosis + constricted pupil = Horner's)

Known smoker, diabetic pt presents with partial ptosis, small pupil and meiosis. Diagnosis is?
   a. 3rd nerve palsy
   b. Diabetic ophthalmopathy
   c. Holmes Adie
   d. Horner syndrome
   **Ans: D**

During thyroidectomy, which of the following is at risk while ligating inferior thyroid artery?
   a. External laryngeal nerve
   b. Internal laryngeal nerve
   c. Superior laryngeal nerve
   d. Recurrent laryngeal nerve
   e. Vagus
   **Ans: D**

A 60- year- old patient reported to the prosthodontist with complaint of inability to place denture into his mouth. The prosthodontist referred the case to the medical specialist, as it was not due to the denture. O/E rigidity and tremors were noted. Which of the following nuclei of brain is involved?
   a. Arcuate Nucleus
   b. Edinger Westphal Nucleus
   *[Page 1 ends]*

## Page 2

1. A pt with Hx of RTA. Presented with fracture fibula neck and foot drop. O/E there is loss of dorsiflexion and loss of sensation over dorsum of the foot. Nerve damaged is?
   a. Superficial peroneal b. Tibial c. Pudendal d. Peroneus longus e. Common peroneal nerve
   **Ans: E**

Mullerian inhibiting factor is produced by?
   a. Theca b. Leydig cells c. Sertoli cells d. G cells e. Ovaries
   **Ans: C**

1. Which of the following is a potent anabolic hormone?
   a. DHEA b. Estrogen c. Progesterone d. Androstenedione e. Testosterone
   **Ans: E** (Note: previously marked C, but corrected to E)

2. A patient admitted in endocrinology ward has the following labs. Potassium: 3 and Na: 150 and pH 7.45. He is most likely having an excess of which hormone?
   a. Cortisol b. Testosterone c. ACTH d. ADH e. Aldosterone
   **Ans: E**

3. Which of the following antibiotics is present on saliva?
   a. Amikacin b. Streptomycin c. Amoxicillin d. Kanamycin e. Erythromycin
   **Ans: E**

Peroxisomes are formed by self- replication by budding off from?
   a. Rough endoplasmic reticulum (RER) b. Golgi apparatus c. Lysosomes d. Mitochondria e. Smooth endoplasmic reticulum (SER)
   **Ans: E**

1. Mode of maternal inheritance of a disease in a new born is via?
   a. Mitochondrial RNA b. Mitochondrial DNA c. Nuclear RNA d. Nuclear DNA e. Golgi apparatus
   **Ans: B**

2. Which immunoglobulin is present in large concentration in serum?
   a. Ig G b. Ig M c. Ig A d. Ig G e. Ig A
   **Ans: A** (IgG)

3. Which is the most potent anti-oxidant?
   a. Vit C b. Transferrin c. Vit D d. Glutathione e. Vit E
   **Ans: D** (Order: Glutathione > Vit E > Transferrin > Vit C > Vit A)

4. Which statement is true regarding Vitamin E?
   a. Carbohydrate metabolism b. Potent antioxidant c. Endothelial protection d. Maintain skin integrity e. Deficiency causes peripheral neuropathy
   **Ans: B**

5. Which type of hypoxia is associated with decreased PO2 and increased A-a gradient?
   a. Anemia b. High altitude c. Emphysema d. Hypoventilation e. Right to left shunt
   **Ans: E**

## Page 4

1. Which of the following is a part of conduction system?
   a. Terminal bronchiole b. Respiratory bronchiole c. Alveoli d. Alveolar ducts

The first heart sound (S1) becomes louder:
   a. In right bundle branch block
   b. In the presence of aortic stenosis
   c. In the presence of mitral insufficiency
   d. When the P-R interval is at the lower limits of normal
   e. When the P-R interval is at the upper limits of normal
   **Ans: D**

1. A 5HT3 antagonist was used in patient with severe abdominal pain and diarrhea. The drug is?
   a. Alosetron b. Diphenoxylate c. Doxycycline d. Hyoscane
   **Ans: A** (Useful in diarrhea-predominant IBS)

2. Commonest type of basal cell carcinoma?
   a. Ulcerated b. Nodular c. Cystic d. Morphoeic e. Pigmented
   **Ans: B**

Which of the following is a cause of edema in known IHD, HTN patient with heart failure?
   a. Increase hydrostatic pressure b. Decrease oncotic pressure c. Increase hypertension d. Increase capillary permeability e. Na retention
   **Ans: A**

The epithelium of preterminal bronchiole is made up of?
   a. Simple cuboidal epithelium b. Stratified squamous without goblet cells c. Simple columnar ciliated epithelium d. Pseudostratified squamous epithelium e. Pseudostratified columnar epithelium
   **Ans: C**

The inability to convert glycolytic into which amino acid leads to kidney stone formation?
   a. Tyrosine b. Alanine c. Tryptophan d. Glycine e. Soluble
   **Ans: D**

1. Which movement of cilia occurs in?
   a. Spermatozoa b. Fallopian tube c. Organ of Corti d. Utrice e. Olfactory membrane
   **Ans: B**

Characteristic sign of cerebellar disease is?
   a. Coarse tremors b. Dysdiokinesia c. Nystagmus d. Dysarthria e. Hypertonia
   **Ans: B** (Sequence: Dysdiokinesia > Dysarthria > Nystagmus > Dysmetria)

Which one of the following is anti- apoptotic?
   a. Bcl-2 b. Bax c. Bak d. Caspases e. Perforins
   **Ans: A**

## Page 5

1. A 71- year- old woman is prescribed ondansetron to help treat nausea which has not responded to either metoclopramide or Cyclizine. What is the mechanism of action of ondansetron?
   a. 5- HT2 antagonist b. Dopamine antagonist at chemoreceptor trigger zone c. NK1 receptor antagonist d. 5- HT3 antagonist e. Antihistamine
   **Ans: D**

2. A 65 year presents with jaundice. On work up Hb 4.5, increase bilirubin, increase retic count 9%. Smear shows Polychromasia and clumps. What test to confirm diagnosis?
   a. Coombs test b. Hb electrophoresis c. Osmotic fragility test d. G6PD e. Bone marrow biopsy
   **Ans: A**

3. Which of the following is derived from 3rd pharyngeal arch?
   a. Cricothyroid b. Stylopharyngeal c. Cricoid d. Stapedius e. Posterior belly of digastric
   **Ans: B**

4. Which pleural layer is completely innervated by phrenic nerve?
   a. Costovertebral pleura b. Diaphragmatic pleura c. Suprapleural membrane d. Costochondral Junction e. Mediastinal pleura
   **Ans: E**

5. The inhaled constituent of the Earth's crust which most consistently produces pulmonary fibrosis is?
   a. Coal b. Iron c. Calcium d. Manganese e. Silica
   **Ans: E**

6. One of the following is known to cause malignancy?
   a. Anthracosis b. Asbestosis c. Berylliosis d. Haemochromatosis e. Silicosis
   **Ans: B**

7. A male presented with generalized skin nodules, marks of scratches on face, loss of hair and eye brows, nasal bridge shortening and gives history of contact. Acid fast bacilli +ve. The biopsy of skin nodule shows the causative agent?
   a. M. Leprae b. M. Tuberculosis c. Syphilis d. M bovis
   **Ans: A**

8. A pregnant lady with labor pains and obstructed labor was taken to the hospital but died before reaching to the hospital. Most likely cause is?
   a. Amniotic fluid embolism b. Fat embolism c. Air embolism d. Pulmonary embolism e. DVT
   **Ans: A**

9. A 45 years old male had automobile accident with fracture of femur. He died after 5 days. Autopsy showed widespread petechiae in cerebral white matter. The most likely cause of death is?
   a. Fat embolism b. Septicaemia c. Adult respiratory distress syndrome d. Countercoup injury e. Subdural hematoma
   **Ans: A**

10. Regarding pia mater:
   a. Extend with dura up to S2 b. Extends into sulci and fissures of brain tissue c. Extends into the ventricles d. Extend in median sulcus e. Extends with arachnoid mater
   **Ans: B**

11. A known HTN lady presented with severe headache (worst headache of life), vomiting and raised ICP. On lumbar puncture, the CSF was blood stained. What is the most likely cause?
   *[Answer not given in original]*

## Page 6

1. Following the use of an oral hypoglycaemic drug, a 50- year male complains of metallic taste in mouth and diarrhea. He was most likely prescribed which drug?
   a. Acarbose b. Glipizide c. Metformin d. Glibenclamide e. Metronidazole
   **Ans: C** (Metformin)

2. 35- year- old female with anterior mediastinal mass is having bilateral ptosis of eye during evening since last few weeks. The underlying mechanism of the disease is?
   a. Immune complex deposition b. Antibodies against ACh Receptor c. Antibodies against host cells d. Antibodies against smooth muscles e. Deficiency of mitochondrial antibodies
   **Ans: B**

3. A newborn baby with erythroblastosis fetalis has the blood group A+. For the exchange transfusion, she must receive the blood having the group?
   a. A+ve b. A-ve c. AB-ve d. B-ve e. O+
   **Ans: B**

4. A 50- year male presents with jaundice. Labs shows increased AST, and liver biopsy reveals presence of Mallory bodies. These findings are highly suggestive of which disease?
   a. Alcoholic fatty liver b. Alcoholic cirrhosis c. Alcoholic hepatitis d. Viral hepatitis e. Primary biliary cirrhosis
   **Ans: C**

5. An admitted patient has been diagnosed with end stage fatal disease. What should the physician do next?
   a. Do not inform the patient b. Inform the family but not the patient c. Inform the patient but divide him to keep it to himself d. Give clear and complete evidence knowledge of gastric based for his benefit e. Start management and inform nobody
   **Ans: D**

6. Autoregulation of kidney is done by?
   a. Myogenic and Tubuloglomerular feedback system b. Feedback system c. Bowman's hydrostatic and Tubuloglomerular feedback system d. Glomerulotubular feedback e. Renin angiotensin aldosterone system f. Capillary hydrostatic pressure with Glomerulotubular feedback mechanism
   **Ans: A**

7. A 4- year girl with no congenital anomaly presents with oedematous body and distended abdomen. O/E hepatosplenomegaly, brittle shiny weak hair, hyperpigmentation, desquamation was noted. What is the most likely diagnosis?
   a. Marasmus b. Beri-Beri c. Vit A intoxication d. Malnutrition e. Kwashiorkor
   **Ans: E**

8. Pharmacokinetic interaction among drugs is exemplified by?
   a. Shortening of action of procaine by adrenaline b. Increase peripheral toxicity of levodopa with carbidopa

## Page 7

1. A 27- year- old woman is given intravenous penicillin to treat infective endocarditis. Within minutes of starting this therapy, she begins to have severe difficulty in breathing and tachypnea. She suddenly develops an erythematous skin rash over most of her body. Her symptoms are most likely to be produced by release of a chemical mediator which is released from?
   a. Heparin b. IgG c. Mast cells d. Monocytes e. Lymphocytes
   **Ans: C**

2. The ECG of a person shows progressively prolongation of PR interval in successive heart beats followed by a drop in beat. The person is most likely to have:
   a. Mobitz type I block b. Mobitz type II block c. Atrial flutter d. Complete A-V block e. First degree A-V block
   **Ans: A**

3. Lymphatic drainage of external nose & anterior part of nasal cavity is from?
   a. Submandibular lymph nodes b. Jugulo-digastric nodes c. Deep cervical lymph nodes d. Retropharyngeal lymph nodes e. Occipital lymph nodes
   **Ans: A**

4. Right shift of the oxygen dissociation curve occurs with?
   a. Decrease pH b. Decrease temperature c. CO poisoning d. Decrease 2,3-DPG
   **Ans: A**

5. A 58- year- old man is admitted to the hospital with acute heart failure and pulmonary edema. Which one of the following drugs given IV would be most useful in treating the pulmonary edema?
   a. Digoxin b. Dobutamine c. Furosemide d. Amiodarone
   *[Answer missing]*

## Page 8

1. In Clavipectoral fascia, which vein is present?
   a. Cephalic b. Basilic c. Axillary d. Subclavian e. Lateral pectoral
   **Ans: A**

2. A patient with TB undergoing treatment presents with complains of inability to differentiate between red and green color. Which of the following drug is responsible for this?
   a. Pyrazinamide b. Rifampicin c. Ethambutol d. Isoniazid e. Streptomycin
   **Ans: C**

3. The slowest growing malignant tumor of the thyroid is:
   a. Papillary carcinoma b. Medullary carcinoma c. Follicular carcinoma d. Anaplastic carcinoma e. Epidermoid carcinoma
   **Ans: A**

Osmotic diuretic acts on?
   a. Thick ascending loop of Henle b. PCT c. Early distal tubules d. Late distal tubules
   **Ans: B**

About 220 students develop fever, body ache, and loss of appetite and yellow discoloration of the eyes. The probable virus causing these symptoms is?
   a. Hep E b. Hep B c. Hep A d. Hep D e. Hep C
   **Ans: C**

1. The test used to best monitor Hepatitis B is?
   a. GGT b. PT c. Serum bilirubin d. Alkaline phosphatase e. SGPT
   **Ans: E**

2. Cysticercosis in human being is caused by ingesting:
   a. Egg of Taenia saginata b. Egg of Taenia solium c. Raw or partly cooked beef d. Raw or partly cooked fish e. Raw or partly cooked mutton
   **Ans: B**

3. Human is intermediate host in:
   a. Beef tapeworm infection b. Filariasis c. Hookworm infection d. Hydatid disease e. Trichomoniasis
   **Ans: D**

The microscopic diagnostic feature of tuberculosis lesion is the presence of:
   a. Langhan's type of multinucleated giant cells b. Localised collection of epithelioid cell c. Localised collection of histiocytes d. Caseating granuloma e. Solid granuloma
   **Ans: D** (Most diagnostic: PCR; #2 AFB > Caseous; Histological: Epithelioid > Caseous; Microscopic: Caseous > Epithelioid; Definitive: Sputum AFB; Characteristic of granuloma: Epithelioid)

1. Referred pain from the appendix will be felt in?
   a. Right iliac fossa b. Left shoulder c. Right shoulder d. Umbilicus e. Left iliac fossa

## Page 9

1. Immediate reversal of Warfarin toxicity is by?
   a. Heparin b. Vit K c. FFP d. Cryoprecipitate e. Protamine sulphate
   **Ans: C** (Vitamin K gives delayed effect, FFP gives immediate effect)

Anterior division from brachial plexus upper and middle trunk combine to form?
   a. Lateral cord b. Posterior cord c. Medial cord d. Lower trunk
   **Ans: A**

Gastrin is released from?
   a. Fundus b. Duodenum c. Gastric antrum d. Pancreas
   **Ans: C**

1. A 35- year- old woman presented with H/o weakness, palpitations and breathlessness on exertion, tingling of feet and difficulty in walking. Her blood examination showed Hb 5g/dl, TLC 3,500/cm, Platelet count 120,000/cm. The most likely diagnosis is:
   a. Aplastic anaemia b. Acute leukemia c. Myelodysplastic syndrome d. Myxedema e. Vitamin B12 deficiency
   **Ans: E**

2. 45- year female delivered a healthy baby with a single palmar crease, hypotonia and depressed nasal bridge. This is likely seen in?
   a. Trisomy 21

## Page 10

1. Regarding Mean:
   a. And median are one and the same thing b. And mode are calculated by same formula c. Is a good measure of the centre of distribution d. Is calculated by totaling the values of all observations and dividing by total number of observations e. Is not same as average
   **Ans: D**

2. A student wanted to study relationship between increases in temperature and duration of surgery. To evaluate results which statistical test he should apply?
   a. Student T test b. ANOVA test c. Mann-Whitney U test d. Regression analysis e. Chi squared
   **Ans: D**

3. Body temperature is regulated mainly by:
   a. Hypothalamus b. Kidney c. Skin d. Lungs e. Pituitary
   **Ans: A**

4. Major phagocytic cell which presents antigen to lymphocyte?
   a. Basophils b. Eosinophils c. Neutrophils d. Histamine e. Monocytes/macrophages
   **Ans: E**

5. A 5- year child presented with history of fever for 2 weeks, epistaxis and diffuse lymphadenopathy. Labs show Hb 5.6, 100x10^9/L and Plt 10x10^9/L. The most likely diagnosis is?
   a. Dengue b. Acute hemorrhagic fever c. Infectious Mononucleosis d. Malaria e. ALL
   **Ans: C**

6. The landmark for pudendal nerve block is?
   a. Sacral promontory b. Ischial spine c. Ischial tuberosity d. Pubic tubercle e. Acetabulum
   **Ans: B**

7. A female pt with chronic renal failure has 5 people who are willing to serve as donor for renal transplant. Her husband, identical twin, half brother, sister and son. The most suitable donor for her will be?
   a. Brother b. Husband c. Step brother d. Identical twin e. Sister
   **Ans: D**

8. An abnormality was sent for age determination regarding the viability of fetus. The fetus was diagnosed to be of negative because of presence of the following feature?
   a. Absence of skin wrinkles b. Absence of toe nails c. Crown rump length > 250mm d. Eyes facing laterally e. Fetal weight 200g
   **Ans: C**

9. Pendant knee jerk occurs in?
   a. UMN b. LMN c. Hypothyroidism d. Cerebellar dysfunction
   **Ans: D**

10. Intention tremors occur due to lesion in?
    a. Internal Capsule b. Cerebellum c. Basal ganglia d. Cerebrum e. Substantia nigra
    **Ans: B**

11. On auscultation the aortic murmur is best heard at?
    a. Left 2nd intercostal space b. Left 4th intercostal space c. Right 2nd intercostal space d. 5th intercostal space
    **Ans: C**

## Page 11

- Aortic area: right 2nd intercostal space
- Pulmonary area: left 2nd intercostal space
- Tricuspid area: left 4th intercostal space
- Mitral area: 5th intercostal space (midclavicular line - apex beat)

    a. CNS Ischemia response b. Chemoreceptors c. Baroreceptors d. RAAS
    **Ans: C**

    a. Non nucleated b. Cytoplasmic granules c. Plug formation when joins collagen fibres d. Platelets changes after splenectomy

1. A 38 years old patient presented in outpatient clinic with complaint of increased thirst, so that he drinks water very frequently. He also complains of increased frequency of micturition. On urine analysis, osmolality of urine was 100 mOsm. The doctor gave him an IV ADH, but his complaints did not improve. The most likely disorder in this patient was?
    a. Central diabetes insipidus b. Nephrogenic diabetes insipidus c. Nephrolithiasis d. Neurogenic bladder e. SIADH
    **Ans: B**

2. The antigen processed by the exogenous epitope proteination pathway are presented with which one of following?
    a. T-cell receptor b. K receptor c. MHC class 2 d. MHC class 1 e. IgG heavy chain
    **Ans: C**

    a. 12th rib mid axillary line b. 11th rib mid clavicular line c. 10th mid axillary line
    *[Answer not clearly given]*

Chagas disease and congenital mega colon affects which layer of GIT?
    a. Serosa b. Mucosa c. Submucosa d. Muscularis mucosa e. Muscularis externa
    **Ans: E**

A middle age female with recurrent chest infections, long history of diarrhea. On stool examination cysts of Giardia lamblia were detected. Peripheral smear reveals no plasma cells. Serum IgA 73, IgG 300 and IgM is 67. What's the most likely diagnosis?
    a. Common variable immunodeficiency b. Bruton's agammaglobulinemia c. HIV infection d. Cystic fibrosis e. Malaria
    **Ans: A**

1. A 20-year-old patient presents with abdominal bloating following meals, severe foul-smelling frothy stools per day. He also complains of weakness. The most appropriate investigation would be:
    a. Stool G and E b. Stool DR c. Barium meal and follow through d. Lipid profile e. Ultrasound of abdomen
    **Ans: B**

2. A 7 years old school going boy develops sore throat. He received antibiotic for it, which resolved it. Following 2 weeks, later he developed generalized body edema, hypertension and hematuria. The most likely diagnosis is?
    a. Nephrotic syndrome b. Drug reaction c. Acute post streptococcal glomerulonephritis d. Bladder stones e. UTI
    **Ans: C**

Hypotension is likely caused by?
    a. Increase in body water b. Decrease in body water c. Absence of ADH d. Decrease in aldosterone level e. Increased salt
    **Ans: A**

## Page 13

1. Antibodies are formed by?
    a. Thymus b. Plasma cells c. Lymphocyte d. Liver e. B cell
    **Ans: B**

2. Short term memory loss occurs due to lesion in?
    a. Hippocampus b. Neocortex c. Amygdala d. Parietal lobe
    **Ans: A**

3. A child presented with abdominal pain and blood in stools, he was diagnosed as a case of gastroenteritis. Which of the following agent is responsible?
    a. Enterotoxigenic E. coli b. Enteropathogenic E. coli c. Enterohemorrhagic E. coli d. Campylobacter jejuni
    **Ans: C**

4. GFR increases with?
    a. Increase thickness of glomerular membrane b. Decrease colloid oncotic pressure c. Increase plasma protein d. Increase oncotic pressure
    **Ans: B**

5. Intercellular connections having protein channels and low electrical resistance are:
    a. Belt desmosomes b. Desmosomes c. Gap junctions d. Tight junctions
    **Ans: C**

6. A patient with hx of Multiple Myeloma has Hypercalcemia, Polyuria and Confusion. Urine Osmolality is 310 mOsm/l. What is the cause of Polyuria?
    a. Decreased ADH formation b. Psychogenic polydipsia c. Decreased action of ADH on collecting tubules d. Increased ADH
    **Ans: C**

7. Receptors act as transducers:
    a. Augmenting the stimuli b. Locally depolarizing channels c. All or none potential d. By increasing response to repeated stimulus
    **Ans: D**

8. A 30- year male presented to ER with chief complaints of persistent retrosternal crushing pain and epigastric pain for 2 to 3 hrs associated with vomiting. On ECG there was ST elevation in anterior limb leads while the cardiac enzymes were normal. The likely diagnosis is:
    a. Pericarditis b. Acute MI c. Retinopathy Embolism d. Pleurisy e. Aortic dissection
    **Ans: B**

9. A 5- year female pt undergoing chemotherapy due to CA breast presented with complaints difficulty in swallowing due to a sore throat. O/E cheesy mucosal plaques in his mouth and white oropharynx pseudohyphae are seen on PAS stain of a mucosal smear. These findings are consistent with diagnosis of?
    a. Cryptococcus b. Histoplasmosis c. Rhinosporidiosis d. Aspergillosis e. Candidiasis
    **Ans: E**

10. Prostaticin is released by:
    a. Hepatocytes b. Macrophages c. Renal tubular cells d. Thrombocytes e. Vascular endothelial cells
    **Ans: E**

11. Which cells contain dense granule and have IgE antibodies on their cell membrane?
    a. Basophils and Eosinophils b. Macrophage c. Lymphocytes d. Monocytes e. Neutrophils
    **Ans: A**

1. If 1L Normal saline solution is infused to a person, then which of the following occurs?
    a. Plasma osmolarity is increased b. Urine osmolarity is increased c. Plasma sodium concentration increased d. Urine osmolarity is decreased
    **Ans: D**

A person loses 1 liter of blood in 5 mins. Which of the following will increase?
    a. Heart rate b. Venous tone c. GFR d. Muscle contraction e. Splanchnic circulation
    **Ans: B**

1. In a patient whose Vasectomy has been done, the composition of ejaculated fluid will be?
    a. Semen b. Seminal fluid without sperm c. Prostatic and seminal fluid d. Prostatic fluid
    **Ans: C**

2. Thirst is stimulated in activation of renin angiotensin system due to?
    a. Angiotensin 2 b. Renin c. Angiotensin 1 d. Aldosterone e. ADH

Regarding human placenta:

## Page 35

1. A pt is infused with PAH to measure RBF. She has a urine flow rate of 1ml/min, plasma PAH of 1mg/ml, urine PAH of 600mg/ml and hematocrit of 45 percent. What is her effective RBF?
    a. 600 ml/min b. 660 ml/min c. 1091 ml/min d. 1333 ml/min
    **Ans: C** (RPF = 1×600/1 = 600; RBF = 600/(1-0.45) = 600/0.55 = 1091)

2. A known CKD, DM patient who is dialysis dependent develops a leg ulcer, the treatment of which requires antibiotics. Which drug can be given without change in dose (renal dose adjustment)?
    a. Cephalosporin b. Imipenem c. Co-amoxiclav d. Meropenem e. Linezolid
    **Ans: D** (Meropenem? Actually linezolid is not renally adjusted; meropenem requires adjustment. Common answer: Linezolid)

3. A Diabetic pt having headache and vomiting with recent history of starting antidepressant (TCA). Labs reveal low sodium level. The likely cause of hyponatremia is?
    a. Psychogenic diabetes mellitus b. SIADH c. Hypercalcemia d. Central DI
    **Ans: B** (TCA can cause SIADH)

4. A young female taking analgesics for backache presented with bleeding gums, epistaxis. She has fever of 101, mild jaundice and hepatosplenomegaly. HB 9.0, TLC 7000, neutropenia, thrombocytopenia and peripheral smear shows immature cells. What is the probable diagnosis?
    a. Acute leukemia b. Drug induced c. CLL d. Aplastic anemia e. Chronic viral hepatitis
    **Ans: A**

5. Which of the following should not be given in myasthenia gravis?
    a. Gentamycin b. Chlorpromazine c. Gold d. Sulfasalazine
    **Ans: B** (Aminoglycosides worsen myasthenia; chlorpromazine also? Classic answer: gentamycin, but option B is chlorpromazine. Possibly B)

6. Neurotransmitter in REM sleep?
    a. Epinephrine b. Serotonin c. Acetylcholine
    **Ans: C**

7. Neurotransmitter in slow wave sleep (NREM)?
    a. Acetylcholine b. Epinephrine c. Dopamine d. Norepinephrine e. Serotonin
    **Ans: E**

8. A 55- year- male presents with right sided headache, visual disturbance. O/E ESR raised, Temporal artery firm, tender and thus biopsied. What is the probable diagnosis?
    a. Takayasu arteritis b. Giant cell Arteritis c. Kawasaki d. Hypertensive arteritis
    **Ans: B**

9. Muscle/structure posterior to the lateral arcuate ligament of diaphragm?
    a. Quadratus lumborum b. Piriformis c. Aorta d. Psoas
    **Ans: A**

10. The ability of the kidney to excrete a concentrated urine will increase if:
    a. The permeability of the proximal tubule to water decreases b. The rate of blood flow through the medulla decreases c. The rate of flow through the loop of Henle increases d. The activity of the Na-K pump in the loop of Henle decreases e. The permeability of the collecting duct to water decreases
    **Ans: B** (Decreased medullary blood flow increases countercurrent multiplication)

## Page 37

1. Diagnostic value for metabolic alkalosis is?
    a. pH < 7.4 b. HCO3 > 24 c. PCO2 > 55 d. PCO2 < 30
    **Ans: B**

2. A patient with severe diarrhea for 3 days presented with tachypnea and respiratory rate 22, hypotension. Labs showed hypochloremia, hyponatremia and hypokalemia with normal bicarbonate. What is the diagnosis?
    a. Metabolic acidosis b. Metabolic alkalosis c. Respiratory acidosis d. Respiratory alkalosis e. Renal tubular acidosis
    **Ans: A** (Non-anion gap metabolic acidosis from diarrhea)

3. As compared to plasma, CSF has?
    a. Hypotonic b. Decreased glucose c. Increased K d. Decreased protein e. Similar pH
    **Ans: B** (CSF glucose is about 60% of plasma)

4. Most important microscopic feature for malignant tumor?
    a. High N/C ratio b. Pleomorphism c. Mitotic figure d. Invasion of basement membrane e. Necrosis
    **Ans: D** (Metastasis > invasion > pleomorphism)

5. Which of the following causes vasoconstriction due to stress of surgery?
    a. Epinephrine b. Norepinephrine c. Serotonin d. ACTH e. GH
    **Ans: A** (Released in stress due to surgery = ACTH; Vasoconstriction due to stress = Epinephrine)

In mountain, the atmospheric pressure 700. Calculate the value of O2 and nitrogen in it?
    a. pO2 110 and pN2 590 b. pO2 100 pN2 600 c. pO2 98 and pN2 602 d. pO2 147 and pN2 546
    **Ans: D** (O2 21% of 700 = 147; N2 78% of 700 = 546)

Refers to the degree to which research findings can be applied to individuals other than those who were studied

## Page 42

1. A patient with jaundice, generalized edema and ascites. The massive accumulation of fluid in abdomen is the result of?
    a. Splenomegaly b. Portal HTN c. Increase water retention d. Increase hydrostatic pressure e. Hypoalbuminemia
    **Ans: B** (Ascites in cirrhosis primarily due to portal HTN)

2. Characteristic sign of cerebellar disease is?
    a. Coarse tremors b. Muscle paralysis c. Nystagmus d. Dysarthria e. Hypertonia
    **Ans: D** (Sequence: Dysdiadochokinesia > Dysarthria > Nystagmus > Dysmetria)

3. Which of the following is caused commonly by UV rays?
    a. Peripheral neuropathies b. Cataract c. Teratogenicity d. Anemia e. Neoplastic changes
    **Ans: B**

4. A 60-year male weighing 70 kg has total body water of 42L (60% of body weight). How much of this will be present in interstitial fluid?
    a. 42L b. 3L c. 11.5L d. 28L e. 12L
    **Ans: C** (Total body water 42L → ICF 28L, ECF 14L; ECF = plasma 3.5L + interstitial 10.5L approx; closest is 11.5L)

A young female presented in OPD with loss of light reflex but intact accommodation reflex. The lesion is at?
    a. Pretectal area b. Oculomotor nerve c. Edinger Westphal nucleus d. Frontal eye field e. Optic nerve
    **Ans: A** (Argyll Robertson pupil → pretectal lesion)

    a. Intestine relaxation b. Hypoglycemia c. Mydriasis d. Bronchodilation e. Vasoconstriction

    a. Thalamus b. Pons c. Hypothalamus d. Medulla e. Amygdala

2. A person has damage to his spinal cord after RTA. What finding will be seen immediately after RTA?
    a. Spasticity b. Flaccidity c. Hypertonia d. Hyperreflexia
    **Ans: B** (Spinal shock → flaccid paralysis initially)

3. A child 5 years old comes to pediatrician with complaint of drowsiness, double vision, headache, vomiting, diarrhea and severe muscle pain, pain more common around neck. Which one of the following suits in differential/provisional diagnosis?
    a. Brain abscess b. Tuberculous meningitis c. Purulent meningitis d. Encephalitis
    **Ans: B**

4. A young boy after coming from school faced RTA & loss of blood in 1 hour. What compensatory mechanism occurs in the boy?
    a. Acute vaso venous tone b. Decrease TPR c. Decrease blood pressure d. Decrease diastolic pressure e. Decrease stroke volume
    **Ans: A**

5. Regarding taste fibres, correct is?
    a. Have tractus solitarius b. Some of the fibers go to tractus solitarius c. Second order neuron to VPM nucleus d. Impulses first run in 7th CN then 5th CN to tractus solitarius

6. DOC for acute gout?
    a. Colchicine b. Propranolol c. Allopurinol d. NSAID

    a. CRH b. Growth hormone c. Prolactin d. Estrogen

6. Postganglionic sympathetic fibers to lacrimal gland carried by?

7. When a person voluntarily deviates his eyes to the left, the cortical efferent pathway comes from his?
    a. Left frontal lobe b. Right occipital lobe c. Left occipital lobe d. Right frontal lobe e. Left temporal lobe
    **Ans: D** (Frontal eye field controls contralateral gaze)

8. A young man has undergone gastrectomy about three months back. His hemoglobin is 6 gm/dl, and presented with pallor weakness and fatigue. The most probable diagnosis is:
    a. Aplastic anaemia b. Hemolytic anaemia c. Megaloblastic anaemia d. Microcytic hypochromic anaemia e. Sickle cell anaemia
    **Ans: C** (Post-gastrectomy B12 deficiency)

On autopsy, a person having cardiac disease have a subendocardial infarct. A circumferential lesion of the left ventricle was noted. The mechanism is?
    a. Cardiac tamponade b. Myocardial shock c. Thrombotic occlusion of LCX d. Pulmonary embolism e. Thrombotic occlusion of RCA
    **Ans: C** (Circumflex artery supplies lateral wall)

Neural crest cells migrate from edges of the neural folds in the hindbrain contribute most likely to the formation of:

2. A young male with certain heart disease presents with exertional SOB and central chest pain. Which drug can be used to relieve the symptoms?

3. A pregnant lady has history of schizophrenia and is on drugs for her disorder. After/during delivery, there is increased production/excretion of milk. Cause of such condition is?

4. A 30 years patient presented in eye OPD with ocular manifestation. On examination, light reflex is absent while accommodation reflex is normal. Cause of lesion is?
    a. Horner syndrome b. Strabismus c. Encephalitis d. Neurosyphilis e. Ptosis

1. A 22- year- old male had mild jaundice. His ALT was raised slightly. Serological tests for viral hepatitis were negative. Examination of the eyes revealed some Kayser-Fleischer rings. Immunological tests were not confirmatory. The most useful investigation in this case would be?
    a. Ceruloplasmin level b. Liver biopsy H & E examination c. PCR for HBV d. PCR for HCV e. Serum copper levels
    **Ans: A** (Wilson disease)

A known HTN patient has increased urine output. This is due to?
    a. Increased glomerular capillary pressure + increased GFR b. Afferent arteriole constriction c. Efferent arteriole dilatation d. Increased hydrostatic pressure in Bowman's capsule and increased GFR
    **Ans: A**

1. Type I hypersensitivity responses of the immune system are accompanied by eosinophilia. An appropriate, useful type I response should most likely be directed against which of the following?
    a. Antigen b. Inhaled dust c. Liver flukes d. Neoplasms e. Spirochetes
    **Ans: C** (Helminth infections)

    a. Galactose b. Lactose c. Fructose d. Pyruvate
    **Ans: D**

    a. Respiratory bronchiole b. Larynx c. Terminal bronchiole d. Trachea e. Bronchi
    **Ans: C**

2. A newborn presents with tetany, serum Calcium 6.3 mg/dl. O/E a pansystolic murmur is heard. A few days later, the newborn develops infections by Pneumocystis carinii, Aspergillus fumigatus and Herpes simplex. He is likely suffering from?
    a. 22q11 deletion syndrome b. Adenosine deaminase deficiency c. B cell lymphoma cell defect can reduce antibodies d. Malaria
    **Ans: A** (DiGeorge syndrome – CATCH 22: Cardiac abnormalities, Abnormal facies, T-cell deficit, Cleft palate, Hypocalcemia, 22q11 microdeletion)

3. Prosopagnosia occurs due to lesion in?
    a. Parietal lobe b. Prefrontal eye field c. Parietal and occipital lobe d. Parieto-occipito-temporal lobe

    a. Secondary somesthetic area b. Parieto-occipital temporal area c. Somatosensory 2 d. Somatosensory 1 e. Somatosensory association area
    **Ans: E**

5. A five years old baby comes with recurrent cervical lymphadenopathy. Klebsiella pneumoniae is isolated on each occasion. He is suffering from which immune deficient state?
    a. Chronic granulomatous disease b. Common variable immunodeficiency c. Severe combined immunodeficiency d. Bruton agammaglobulinemia
    **Ans: A** (X-linked, NADPH oxidase defect; organisms are ingested but not killed)

1. A HTN pt was started on captopril (ACE inhibitor). ACE inhibitors increase renin and bradykinin. By which mechanism does this drug increase bradykinin levels?
    a. Inhibit conversion of angiotensin 1 to angiotensin 2 b. Inhibit Kallikrein mechanism c. Stimulate Kallikrein mechanism d. Decrease cardiac output
    **Ans: B** (ACE also breaks down bradykinin; inhibition → increased bradykinin)

2. A 40-year-old previously healthy woman, a non-smoker, had episodes of fever, non-productive cough and dyspnea over the past 3 months. Her symptoms disappeared after a month's vacation, but reappeared when she returned home to take care of her canaries. On physical examination there are no abnormal findings. A chest radiograph shows nodular infiltrates in all lung fields. Her disease is most likely to be produced via which of the following mechanisms?
    a. Antigen-antibody complex formation b. Infection with Mycobacterium kansasii c. Langerhans cell proliferation d. Mast cell degranulation e. Progressive interstitial fibrosis
    **Ans: A** (Hypersensitivity pneumonitis, Type III reaction)

3. Type of hypersensitivity reaction in Systemic lupus erythematosus (SLE) is?
    a. Type 1 b. Type 2 c. Type 3 d. Type 4
    **Ans: C** (Immune complex mediated)

4. A 38-week pregnant woman visited her family in a remote area having an epidemic disease after which she develops jaundice suddenly. Which type of hepatitis is most likely prevalent in the pregnant women?
    a. Hep E b. Hep A c. Hep B d. Hep C e. Hep D
    **Ans: A** (HEV is lethal in pregnancy)

## Page 63

- Most common hepatitis: HAV
- Remote area: HEV
- Highest mortality rate (20%): HDV
- Lethal in pregnancy: HEV
- Oro-fecal spread: HAV > HEV
- Hepatocellular carcinoma: HBV > HCV (in Pakistan, Hep C is most common cause)
- Hepatitis B associated with: Polyarteritis nodosa, Aplastic anemia
- Hepatitis C associated with: NHL, ITP, autoimmune hemolytic anemia

3. A girl presented with persistent cough with thick mucus, wheezing and repeated lung infections. She is also having petechiae all over body and has bleeding tendency. She is diagnosed with cystic fibrosis. Which vitamin is deficient in this case?
    a. Vit A b. Vit K c. Vit D d. Vit C e. Vit B6

4. A fisherman after a burn was brought to ER. Which of the following electrolyte imbalances causes a decrease in the height and slope of action potential?
    a. Hyperkalemia b. Hypokalemia c. Hypernatremia d. Hyponatremia e. Hypocalcemia

    a. Cryptosporidium species b. Naegleria fowleri c. Entamoeba histolytica d. Leishmania donovani e. Plasmodium falciparum

Pneumotaxic center functions primarily to:
    a. Decrease the rate of respiration b. Discharge inspiratory potential c. Initiate inspiration from signal d. Limit the respiration e. Prolong the respiration
    **Ans: D**

1. Regarding inhibitors and promoters causing carcinoma?
    a. Only initiators cause carcinoma b. Only promoters cause carcinoma c. Initiators followed by promoters cause carcinoma d. Promoters followed by initiators
    **Ans: C**

    a. Subepithelial humps b. Subendothelial humps c. Massive proteinuria d. WBC casts in urine
    **Ans: C** (Nephrotic syndrome)

    a. Bacillus cereus

1) Sublingual nitroglycerin absorbed immediately in:

    **Ans: B**

    **Ans: D**

3) Right atrium infarction involves which of following?
    a. Septomarginal band b. Moderator band c. Pectinate muscle d. Papillary muscle e. Trabeculae
    **Ans: C**

4) Posterior external arcuate fibers are other name for which of the following?
    a. Anterior spinocerebellar b. Posterior spinocerebellar c. Spinothalamic tract d. Dorsal column e. Cuneocerebellar tract
    **Ans: E**

5) A patient with bronchogenic carcinoma posterior to left lung hilum – which structure is likely to be damaged?
    a. Phrenic nerve b. Vagus nerve c. Esophagus d. Recurrent Laryngeal nerve e. Brachiocephalic trunk
    **Ans: B**

**Explanation:**

- Azygos vein anterior to right root of lung
- Aorta posterior to left root of lung
- Phrenic nerve anterior to root of lung
- Vagus nerve posterior to root of lung

Patient is taking warfarin and starting to bleed – what is treatment?
    a. Heparin b. Aspirin c. TPA d. Fibrinogen e. Vitamin K
    **Ans: E > D** (Immediate reversal: Prothrombin complex concentrate or FFP; Long term antidote: Vitamin K)

Pituitary tumor invades which bone?
    a. Frontal bone b. Sphenoid body c. Cribriform plate d. Ethmoid e. Temporal
    **Ans: B**

1) A lady presented with tremors while writing. She has no other symptoms but her sister complains of similar problem. Which drug should be given?
    a. Amitriptyline b. Ropinirole c. Adrenaline d. Amantadine e. Propranolol
    **Ans: E** (Essential tremor)

2) Smell of burnt urine is present in:
    a. Phenylketonuria b. Alkaptonuria c. Maple Syrup urine disease d. McArdle disease
    **Ans: C** (Maple syrup urine disease)

3) 72 year old patient has history of tongue bite. Which nerve carries taste on the anterior 2/3rd of the tongue?
    a. Lingual b. Glossopharyngeal c. Vagus d. Hypoglossal e. Chorda tympani
    **Ans: E**

**Explanation:**

- Anterior 2/3 general sensation: Lingual nerve
- Anterior 2/3 taste sensation: Chorda tympani
- Posterior 1/3 taste sensation: Glossopharyngeal nerve
- Posterior most part taste sensation: Vagus

## Page 3

1) Strongest stimulus for erythropoietin is:
    a. Hypoxia b. Injury c. Increased pH d. Decreased pH e. Lactate
    **Ans: A**

2) Aspirin decreases fever by decrease in which of following?
    a. Prostaglandins b. Leukotrienes c. Histamine d. Infection e. Prostacyclin
    **Ans: A**

3) Blow to head caused extradural hematoma due to involvement of which artery?
    a. Middle meningeal artery b. Anterior cerebral artery c. Posterior cerebral artery d. Superior cerebral veins e. Bridging veins
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- Middle meningeal artery: epidural hematoma (lucid interval, biconvex, does not cross suture lines)
- Bridging veins: subdural hematoma (no lucid interval, crosses suture lines)

1) Which part of intestine has thick loop with less mesentery fat and long vasa recta with few arcades – surgeon asked resident by uplifting of gut during surgery?
    a. Duodenum b. Jejunum c. Ileum d. Colon e. Rectum
    **Ans: B**

| Feature | Jejunum | Ileum |
|---------|---------|-------|
| Color | Deeper red | Paler pink |
| Wall | Thick and heavy | Thin and light |
| Vascularity | Greater | Lesser |
| Vasa recta | Few long | Many small |
| Mesentery fat | Less | More |
| Lymphoid nodules | Few | Many (Peyer's patches) |
| Plicae circulares | Large & tall | Low & sparse |

1) Structure with longitudinal muscles in adventitia is?
    a. Large size vein b. Muscular artery c. Medium size vein d. Small size vein
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- Muscular artery: three layers thick muscle, adventitia, internal lamina
- Large size vein: smooth muscles longitudinally arranged in adventitia

1) Patient had RTA, result in damage above sacral spinal level. That will lead to:
    a. Automatic Bladder b. Atonic Bladder c. Neurogenic Bladder d. Autonomous Bladder
    **Ans: A** (Spastic/automatic bladder)

## Page 5

1) A patient with Androgen Insensitivity Syndrome is undergoing laparotomy. During dissection at ovarian fossa, ovary attached to lateral pelvic wall – which artery is at risk of damage?
    a. Obturator b. Internal iliac c. Uterine d. Superior mesenteric e. Superior epigastric
    **Ans: B**

During hysterectomy, surgeon must know what important relation about ureter?
    a. Passes in front of uterine artery b. Behind the internal iliac c. At pelvic brim d. Pass behind the broad ligament e. At bifurcation of iliac vessels
    **Ans: D**

**Explanation:** During hysterectomy, ureter damage occurs at:

- Cardinal ligament (uterine vessel) – most common
- Behind broad ligament
- At pelvic brim (ovarian artery)

Ureter damage at pelvic brim – while crossing common iliac vessel:

- Anterior to ureter: gonadal vessel
- Posterior to ureter: iliac vessel

1) Structure present behind ovary and ureter:
    a. Internal iliac artery b. Uterine artery c. Testicular artery d. Ovarian artery
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:** Ovarian fossa boundaries:

- Superior: external iliac vein and artery
- Anterior: broad ligament of uterus

    a. Anterior hypothalamus b. Posterior hypothalamus c. Lateral hypothalamus d. Medial hypothalamus e. Thalamus
    **Ans: B**

**Explanation:**

- Posterior hypothalamus: activated by cold → sympathetic → heat generation
- Anterior hypothalamus: activated by hot → parasympathetic → cooling
- Overall temperature regulation: Preoptic nucleus > Anterior hypothalamus

    **Ans: A**

- Specificity (true negative): detects non-disease, rules in disease (associated with true negative and false positive)

3) Most important feature of platelet is:
    a. Plug formation b. Granules c. No nucleus d. Derived from bone marrow
    **Ans: A**

4) First line of defense in bleeding is:
    a. Vasoconstriction
    **Ans: A** (Primary hemostasis: vasoconstriction then platelet plug)

## Page 23

1) Which of the following occurs due to sympathetic stimulation?
    a. Ciliary muscle contraction b. Bronchoconstriction c. Bradycardia d. Bronchodilation e. Miosis
    **Ans: D**

Pregnant lady with labor pain for 2h develops dyspnea and dies within 15 min. Most likely cause is:
    a. Pulmonary Embolism b. Amniotic fluid embolism c. Fat embolism d. MI e. Air Embolism
    **Ans: B**

1) Most appropriate route for antidote:
    a. IM b. IV c. SC d. Oral e. Rectal
    **Ans: B**

2) Benzodiazepines, barbiturates and other anticonvulsants work by acting on which neurotransmitter?
    a. GABA b. Glutamate c. Acetylcholine d. Glycine e. Epinephrine
    **Ans: A**

A patient presented with hepatitis viral markers negative, ALT slightly raised. On examination there were Kayser-Fleischer rings seen. What is the suitable diagnostic test?
    a. Serum ceruloplasmin b. Urinary copper c. HBsAg d. Anti-mitochondrial antibody
    **Ans: A**

## Page 24

[Scanned with CamScanner – no content]

## Page 25

1) A 53 year old lady is concerned about her strong family history of Breast Cancer and IHD. Her sister died of MI. She is also concerned about osteoporosis. Which prophylaxis drug will you give for post-menopausal related osteoporosis?
    a. Bisphosphonates b. Tamoxifen c. Raloxifene d. HRT e. Calcium and Vitamin D
    **Ans: C** (Raloxifene – SERM for osteoporosis prevention in postmenopausal women)

2) Which of following is most aggressive carcinoma?
    a. BCC b. SCC c. Melanoma d. Leukoplakia e. Lichen planus
    **Ans: C**

**Explanation:**

- Most common pre-malignant lesion: Leukoplakia
- Most lethal pre-malignant lesion: Erythroplakia
- Most common pre-malignant condition: Submucosal fibrosis
- Most lethal pre-malignant condition: Lichen planus
- Most aggressive carcinoma: Melanoma

1) Lowest maternal mortality in which age group?
    a. 10-20 b. 20-30 c. 30-40 d. 40-50
    **Ans: B**

2) Type of necrosis in pancreatitis:
    a. Fat necrosis b. Coagulative necrosis c. Caseous necrosis d. Liquefactive necrosis e. Fibrinoid necrosis
    **Ans: A**

Primigravida visits remote area, AST, ALT raised, jaundice. Diagnosis is:
    a. Hep. A b. Hep. E c. Hep. B d. Hep. D e. Hep. C
    **Ans: B**

**Explanation:**

- Orofecal route: Hep A > Hep E
- Most lethal hepatitis: Hep D
- Most common in pregnancy: Hep A
- Most lethal/remote area in pregnancy: Hep E
- Most common virus after blood transfusion: CMV > Hep B > Hep C
- Most common sexual spread: Hep B
- HCC: Hep B > Hep C
- Cirrhosis: Hep C > Hep B
- Needle stick injury risk: Hep B (30%) > C (3%) > HIV (0.3%)
- Hep A & E: naked viruses

Which drug is used in headache and contraindicated in peripheral vascular disease?
    a. Aspirin b. Ergometrine c. Celecoxib d. Sumatriptan
    **Ans: B**

Patient presented with painful leg ulcer and having Howell-Jolly bodies on smear. What is likely diagnosis?
    a. Hemolytic anemia b. Sickle cell anemia c. Pernicious anemia d. Hereditary spherocytosis
    **Ans: B**

A patient with H/O 3rd degree burn destroying stratum corneum, spinosum and lucidum. Acute loss will lead to:
    a. Acute water loss b. Pressure sensation loss c. Sebum loss d. Hair follicle rupture e. Temperature loss
    **Ans: A**

Female urethra:
    a. Lies below diaphragm b. Lies below urogenital diaphragm c. Lies below urogenital triangle
    **Ans: B**

## Page 28

**Laryngeal muscle functions:**

| Action | Muscles |
|--------|---------|
| Adduct vocal cord / close glottis | Lateral cricoarytenoid (main), Transverse arytenoids (main), Thyroarytenoids |
| Tense vocal cord | Cricothyroid |
| Relax vocal cord | Thyroarytenoid, Vocalis |
| Open larynx inlet | Thyroepiglotticus |
| Close larynx inlet | Aryepiglotticus, Oblique arytenoid |

1) Which of the following tract carries sensation of pain and temperature?
    a. DCML b. Anterior Spinothalamic Tract c. Lateral spinothalamic Tract d. Corticospinal Tract e. Rubrospinal Tract
    **Ans: C**

**Explanation:**

- Dorsal column medial lemniscus: proprioception, vibration, fine touch, two-point discrimination
- Anterior spinothalamic: crude touch
- Lateral spinothalamic: pain & temperature

1) Organ lined by stratified squamous epithelium with increased vascularity, elasticity, tubular glands in lamina propria?
    a. Vagina b. Uterus c. Fallopian tube d. Cervix e. Ureter
    **Ans: A**

A patient with swelling in neck, bilateral exophthalmos and antithyroid antibodies and raised T3 and T4. Likely due to:
    a. Graves' disease b. Hashimoto's c. Goiter d. Thyrotoxicosis
    **Ans: A**

A postpartum lady wants to feed her baby. Which hormone helps her?
    a. GnRH b. Cortisol c. Estrogen + Progesterone d. Prolactin e. ACTH
    **Ans: D**

1) Daily requirement of protein according to FDA is:
    a. 3gm/kg b. 1gm/kg c. 5gm d. 15gm e. 20gm
    **Ans: B**

2) Pathological deficit in malignant hyperthermia is:
    a. Sarcoplasmic Ca tubules b. Ryanodine receptors c. Cell receptors d. Cell membrane e. Nuclear receptor
    **Ans: B**

3) Common cyanotic heart disease is:
    a. ASD b. VSD c. TOF d. PDA e. Eisenmenger
    **Ans: C**

**Explanation:**

- Most common congenital/acyanotic disorder in child: VSD
- Most common acyanotic disorder in adults: ASD
- Most common congenital cyanotic disorder: TOF
- Most common congenital cyanotic anomaly at birth: TGA
- Female living at high altitude or premature baby: PDA
- Cyanotic heart disease in which shunt is necessary for survival: TGA

## Page 29

1) A patient blindfolded, asked to identify the structure in hand. Which assessment is being done?
    a. Primary somesthetic area b. Secondary somesthetic area c. Somesthetic association area d. DCML association area e. Primary motor area
    **Ans: C** (Stereognosis – somesthetic association area)

A patient unable to recognize faces (prosopagnosia). Area injured is:
    a. Parietal b. Parieto-temporal lobe c. Somesthetic area d. Frontal lobe e. Occipital lobe
    **Ans: B**

**Explanation:**

- Asterognosis: parietal lobe, somesthetic association area > primary somatosensory
- Prosopagnosia: inferior temporal lobe

1) Anti-tumor cells is which of following?
    a. Neutrophils b. NK cells c. Macrophages d. Basophil e. Eosinophil
    **Ans: B**

2) Ejaculation occurs due to which of following?
    a. Pudendal nerve b. Sympathetic c. Parasympathetic d. Obturator nerve
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- Overall ejaculation: Pudendal nerve > Sympathetic
- Emission: Sympathetic
- Ejection: Pudendal
- Erection: Parasympathetic

Iron requirement in pregnant female:
    a. 500 mg b. 1500 mg c. 1000 mg d. 2000 mg e. 1200 mg
    **Ans: C**

1) A patient presented after RTA, you are advised to make histology slide containing muscle fasciculus surrounded by connective tissue. The layer is termed as:
    a. Perimysium b. Epimysium c. Endomysium d. Myofibril e. Myocyte
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- Epimysium: encloses entire muscle
- Endomysium: encloses single muscle fiber
- Perimysium: encloses bundle of muscle fibers (fasciculus)
- Endoneurium: individual nerve fiber
- Perineurium: bundle of nerve fibers
- Epineurium: entire nerve

Acrosome reaction occurs when sperm binds with?
    a. Corona radiata of egg b. Zona pellucida of egg c. Corpus oophorum d. None
    **Ans: B**

1) During menstruation and parturition, which layer is shed?
    a. Functionalis b. Basalis c. Functionalis and basalis d. Basalis and endometrium e. Endometrium + superficial myometrium
    **Ans: A**

2) Beta HCG most important function is:
    a. Maintains corpus luteum b. Formation of male sex hormone c. Descent of testes d. Maintain female androgenic hormone e. Maintain placenta
    **Ans: A**

## Page 30

1) Most important test to differentiate beta thalassemia from iron deficiency anemia is:
    a. Serum ferritin b. TIBC c. HbF d. HbA2
    **Ans: D** (Increased HbA2 in beta thalassemia trait)

2) Which one is directly involved in opsonization?
    a. C3b b. C6a c. C4a d. C2
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- Opsonization: C3b & IgG
- Phagocytosis: Neutrophil
- Chemotactic factor for phagocytosis: C5a

1) In which phenomenon do we see increased CO2, decreased TPR and increased vasodilation in skeletal muscle?
    a. CO poisoning b. Cyanide Poisoning c. Hypoxia d. Exercise
    **Ans: D**

2) Pregnancy is stuck at which phase of menses?
    a. Progestational b. Ovulation c. Premenstrual d. Follicular Phase
    **Ans: D**

3) Which of the following is causative agent of carcinoma cervix?
    a. HPV 16 b. CMV c. EBV d. HHV 8 e. HSV
    **Ans: A**

4) What's the most common cause of cervical dysplasia, causing cervical carcinoma?
    a. CMV b. Multiparity c. HSV d. EBV e. HPV
    **Ans: E**

5) Rigor mortis is due to:
    a. Increased ATP b. Decreased ATP c. Increased Calmodulin levels d. Decreased Ca e. Increased phosphate
    **Ans: B**

6) A dead body after 8h in rigor mortis is due to:
    a. Increased phosphate b. Separation of actin-myosin bridges c. Unbroken actin-myosin cross bridges d. Failure of troponin to contract
    **Ans: C**

**Explanation:** ATP is needed to separate actin-myosin cross bridges. After death, no ATP → no separation.

1) During anaphylactic shock, histamine is released from:
    a. Plasma cells b. Mast cells c. Basophils d. Neutrophils e. Macrophages
    **Ans: B**

2) Gestational sac is also called:
    a. Embryo b. Fetus c. Amniotic Sac d. Development Sac
    **Ans: C**

3) A patient was given Atracurium. It leads to hypotension by:
    a. Increased CO b. Decreased Venous return c. Hypoxia d. Histamine release
    **Ans: D**

4) A young boy having mass in neck. Biopsy of lymph node shows effaced architecture, atypical mononuclear cells with bilobed nucleus and CD30 positive. Diagnosis is:
    a. Non-Hodgkin lymphoma b. Hodgkin lymphoma c. T cell leukemia d. Infectious mononucleosis e. Burkitt lymphoma
    **Ans: B** (Reed-Sternberg cell – bilobed, CD15 and CD30 positive)

## Page 31

Inferior rectal artery is branch of:
    a. SMA b. Celiac artery c. Inferior mesenteric d. Internal pudendal e. Internal iliac
    **Ans: D**

**Explanation:**

- Superior rectal branch: Inferior mesenteric artery
- Middle rectal branch: Internal iliac artery
- Inferior rectal branch: Internal pudendal artery

After an automobile accident, splenectomy done. After two months, patient presents to emergency with septic shock and fever. Causative organism for this overwhelming infection is:
    a. Klebsiella b. Mycoplasma c. Pseudomonas d. Staph aureus e. Streptococcus pneumoniae
    **Ans: E** (Overwhelming post-splenectomy infection – encapsulated organisms)

Most common cause of sub-acute bacterial endocarditis is?
    a. S. aureus b. S. viridans c. Enterococcus d. Pseudomonas e. Streptococcus
    **Ans: B** (Strep. viridans)

**Explanation:**

- Acute endocarditis (no pre-existing heart disease): Staph aureus
- Subacute endocarditis (with pre-existing heart disease): Strep viridans

Low testosterone level is present in:
    a. Infant b. Old age c. Preschool d. Neonate
    **Ans: C**

Non-insulin dependent diabetic and hypertensive female patient had cholecystectomy. On the 3rd post-operative day, she complained of sudden onset of dyspnea, chest pain and hemoptysis. The most likely cause would be:
    a. Myocardial infarction b. Pneumonia c. Pulmonary embolism d. Septicemia e. Spontaneous pneumothorax
    **Ans: C**

A baby has some cardiac abnormality with a machinery murmur on auscultation. What is the abnormality?
    a. PDA b. TOF c. VSD d. ASD e. TGA
    **Ans: A**

A patient Para 8 with uterine prolapse and cervix at introitus. Which ligament is damaged?
    a. Uterosacral ligament b. Transverse cervical ligament c. Broad ligament d. Round ligament e. Perineal body
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- 1st degree: descent of cervix within vagina
- 2nd degree: descent of cervix to introitus
- 3rd degree: descent of cervix outside introitus
- 4th degree (procidentia): whole uterus outside introitus
- In 1st and 2nd degree: uterosacral ligament damage
- In 3rd degree: uterosacral > cardinal ligament damage
- In 4th degree: cardinal ligament damage

## Page 32

1) Decrease in size of uterus after 10 days of delivery is to 5-10g. What would it be after 6-8 weeks?
    a. 100g b. 500g c. 60g d. 200g
    **Ans: C**

**Explanation:** Uterus weight:

- After delivery: 1000g
- After 1 week: 500g
- After 2 weeks: 300-350g
- After 4 weeks: 100g
- After 6-8 weeks (involution complete): 40-60g

1) For increasing iron absorption, what should be added in diet?
    a. Vegetable b. Pulses c. Citrus fruit d. Meat e. Egg
    **Ans: C** (Vitamin C enhances iron absorption)

2) A surgeon while doing oophorectomy has to ligate ureter. Which artery is prone to damage with ureter?
    a. Common iliac b. External iliac c. Pudendal d. Internal iliac
    **Ans: D**

3) A day following hysterectomy, patient complains of severe pain in the right upper lumbar region of the back. Which of the following structures was most likely damaged during the surgery?
    a. Inferior mesenteric artery b. Internal iliac artery c. Psoas major muscle d. Pudendal nerve e. Ureter
    **Ans: E**

4) Patient underwent hysterectomy. Damage can occur to ureter at which location?
    a. Pelvic brim b. 2cm from ischial spine c. Behind Broad ligament d. When crossing common iliac artery e. At bifurcation of iliac vessels
    **Ans: C**

**Explanation:** During hysterectomy, ureter damage occurs at:

- Cardinal ligament (uterine vessel) – most common
- Behind broad ligament
- At pelvic brim (ovarian artery)

Ureter damage at pelvic brim – while crossing common iliac vessel:

- Anterior to ureter: gonadal vessel
- Posterior to ureter: iliac vessel
- While removing ovary: damage to internal iliac artery

At examination of cervix, which ligament can be touched?
    a. Pubosacral b. Pubovesical c. Uterosacral d. Broad ligament
    **Ans: C**

1) Star shaped lumen is related to which of following?
    a. Ureter b. Esophagus c. Fallopian tube d. Arteries e. Esophagus
    **Ans: A** (Ureter has stellate lumen in cross-section)

2) A patient smokes daily, presents with chronic cough, sputum and diagnosed as chronic bronchitis. Which will be seen in chronic bronchitis?
    a. Hyperplasia of mucus secreting cells b. Squamous metaplasia c. Atrophy of mucus secreting cells d. Hyperplasia of serous cells
    **Ans: A**

3) 7 month pregnant lady with chronic ITP having ecchymosis, platelets 50,000 and on full steroid dose. What will be next suitable step?
    a. IV immunoglobulin b. Immunosuppressants c. Splenectomy d. Plasmapheresis
    **Ans: A**

## Page 33

A patient having scaly dermatitis, cheilosis and gingivitis. Likely deficiency of:
    a. Vitamin K b. Vitamin A c. Vitamin B9 d. Vitamin C
    **Ans: D** (Scurvy – Vitamin C)

Differentiate between Rickettsia and Mycoplasma by which of following?
    a. Ziehl-Neelsen stain b. Gram stain c. Sudan black d. Giemsa stain
    **Ans: D** (Giemsa stain)

Female with hard cystic swelling between labia majora and labia minora due to which gland involvement?
    a. Greater Vestibular gland b. Bulbospongiosus muscle c. Bulbourethral gland d. Bartholin cyst e. Cervical gland
    **Ans: D** (Bartholin's cyst)

MOA of theophylline is:
    a. Bronchoconstriction b. Alpha agonist c. ACE inhibitor d. Venodilator e. Phosphodiesterase inhibition
    **Ans: E**

Cabergoline MOA is:
    a. B1 agonist b. B2 agonist c. D1 agonist d. D2 agonist
    **Ans: D**

A young male had an RTA which resulted in a femur fracture. He died 5 days later. Autopsy showed cerebral petechiae. Diagnosis is:
    a. Sepsis b. Fat embolism c. Pulmonary embolism d. Myocardial dysfunction
    **Ans: B**

A newborn is brought with lumbosacral swelling containing meninges without neural tissue. What is most likely diagnosis?
    a. Spina bifida with Meningocele b. Meningomyelocele c. Encephalocele d. Meningomyeloencephalocele e. Anencephaly
    **Ans: A**

A woman having urinary tract infection came with fever, pneumonia and BP 80/60 mmHg. She goes into shock. What is the mechanism of her shock?
    a. Neurogenic b. Septic c. Anaphylactic d. Hypotensive
    **Ans: B**

Insulin injection given in DKA. Most immediate response is:
    a. Increased blood potassium b. Increased urinary ketones c. Hyperglycemia d. Increased CO2 e. Increased pH
    **Ans: E** (Insulin corrects acidosis)

Mechanism of cancer formation:
    a. Initiator and promotor b. Only initiator causes carcinoma c. Initiator followed by promotor causes carcinoma d. Multiple initiators e. Promotor followed by initiator
    **Ans: C**

## Page 41

1) Which one is phagocytic?
    a. Juxtaglomerular cell b. Erythropoietin c. Mesangial cell d. Peritubular cell
    **Ans: C**

A blood group has which of following?
    a. Anti B antibodies b. Anti A antibodies c. No antibodies d. AB antibodies
    **Ans: A** (Blood group A has anti-B antibodies)

Diagnostic criteria for bronchial asthma:
    a. FEV1 > 65 b. FEV1/FVC < 65% c. FEV1 zero d. FEV1/FVC normal e. FVC normal
    **Ans: B**

1) Artery palpated between trachea and infrahyoid is:
    a. Internal carotid b. Common carotid c. Internal jugular vein d. External Carotid
    **Ans: B**

2) A patient after fall on outstretched hand with trauma on wrist develops dislocation of lower portion of joint posteriorly and medially. Most probably he has?
    a. Fracture of neck of scaphoid bone b. Fracture of lunate c. Colles Fracture d. Fracture of ulna e. Fracture of metacarpal bone
    **Ans: C**

3) Patient brought to ER unconscious, there is breathing problem. Empty bottle of aspirin found. Which one eliminates aspirin from body?
    a. Bicarbonate administration b. NH4Cl administration c. IV hydration d. Diuretic administration e. Gastric lavage
    **Ans: A** (Alkalinization of urine increases aspirin excretion)

Cheilosis and corneal vascularization is due to deficiency of which vitamin?
    a. Thiamine b. Biotin c. Riboflavin d. Folate e. Vitamin C
    **Ans: C**

**Explanation:**

- B1 deficiency: Dry beriberi, wet beriberi, Wernicke-Korsakoff (measured by transketolase)
- B2 deficiency: Corneal vascularization, cheilosis
- B3 deficiency: Pellagra (diarrhea, dementia, dermatitis)
- B5: Co-factor for CoA, deficiency → adrenal insufficiency
- B7 (Biotin): Binds avidin, one-carbon carrier, role in liver metabolism
- B9 (Folic acid): One-carbon transfer, deficiency → NTD
- B12 deficiency: Megaloblastic anemia

Left circumflex artery supplies which area?
    a. Right Ventricle b. Right atrium c. Left ventricular d. Left atrium and left ventricle e. Inferior wall
    **Ans: D** (LCX supplies left atrium and left ventricle lateral wall)

A child previously having TB comes with complaint of fever and cough along with noisy breathing and difficulty in swallowing, now diagnosed with retropharyngeal abscess. Which structure will it invade first?
    a. Pre-cervical fascia b. Prevertebral fascia c. Carotid sheath d. Buccopharyngeal fascia
    **Ans: B**

Moderate hemorrhage can be diagnosed clinically as:
    a. Supine tachycardia
    **Ans: A** (Postural dizziness, supine tachycardia)

## Medicine 20 August Afternoon

1) After myocardial injury, what biochemical changes will be seen in hypoxia?
    a. Aerobic Glycolysis b. Oxidative Phosphorylation c. Anaerobic Glycolysis + Glycogenesis d. Gluconeogenesis
    **Ans: C**

2) A patient after 1 year of gastrectomy has anemia, fatigue and raised MCV 110. He is also having peripheral numbness and tingling sensation. Which type of anemia is he suffering from?
    a. Pernicious anemia b. Iron deficiency anemia c. Thalassemia d. Anemia of chronic disease e. Sideroblastic anemia
    **Ans: A** (If no option of B12 deficiency or megaloblastic anemia, prefer this)

3) Child awakes from sleep and starts walking. It is termed as:
    a. Somnolence b. Somnambulism c. Somniloquy d. Hypnagogism
    **Ans: B**
    - Sleep walking: Somnambulism
    - Sleep talking: Somniloquy

4) A woman had a polyp in the cervix. It was removed and histopathology showed a portion of the polyp covered by squamous epithelium. The change is:
    a. Anaplasia b. Hypertrophy c. Metaplasia d. Hyperplasia e. Dysplasia
    **Ans: C**

5) A 29 year female presents with lethargy and irritability for the last 5 years. Labs revealed Hb of 9.6, MCV 70 and MCHC low with normal WBC and PLT count. She was prescribed iron supplements yet after 2 months she has Hb 10.2. Which lab investigations should be ordered to find the underlying cause of persistent anemia?
    a. Total iron binding capacity b. Hb electrophoresis c. Reticulocyte count d. Ferritin levels e. Bone marrow biopsy
    **Ans: B** (Thalassemia trait vs IDA)

6) Decreased K excretion is due to:
    a. Aldosterone b. Metabolic acidosis c. Prolonged vomiting d. Diarrhea e. Renal failure
    **Ans: B > E**

**Explanation:** Renal failure leads to metabolic acidosis → H+ moves into cells, K+ moves out → hyperkalemia → decreased tubular excretion.

1) After diapedesis, cytokines involved in neutrophil migration is:
    a. C5a b. C5b c. C3b + IgG d. FC portion of C3B e. C3a
    **Ans: A**

2) Correct sequence of events for neutrophil migration toward the site of acute inflammation is:
    a. Margination, adhesion, rolling, transmigration b. Margination, rolling, adhesion, transmigration c. Rolling, adhesion, margination, transmigration d. Transmigration, rolling, adhesion, margination
    **Ans: B**

## Page 5

1) Hormone responsible for glycolysis, gluconeogenesis and ketogenesis:
    a. Insulin b. Glucagon c. Cortisol d. Prolactin e. Thyroid hormone
    **Ans: B**

2) Intrahepatic protein anabolism and extrahepatic catabolism:
    a. Insulin b. Glucagon c. Cortisol d. Prolactin e. Thyroid hormones
    **Ans: C**

3) A 10 year boy diagnosed with tapeworm infestation. The drug of choice is:
    a. Ciprofloxacin b. Mebendazole c. Niclosamide d. Metronidazole e. Pyrantel pamoate
    **Ans: C**

4) Least dilatable part of the urethra is:
    a. Membranous part b. Prostatic part c. Spongy d. All are equally dilatable e. External urethral meatus
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- External urethral meatus: narrowest part
- Prostatic urethra: widest and most distensible
- Membranous urethra: shortest and least dilatable

1) Bone marrow biopsy is done by:
    a. Ventral iliac crest b. Pubis c. Ischium d. Ischial tuberosities
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- First: Posterior iliac crest (most accessible)
- Second: Anterior superior iliac crest (especially in obese)
- Third: Spinous process of lumbar vertebrae
- Fourth: Tibia (in <1 year, medial aspect of upper end)
- Fifth: Sternum (manubrium or first part of body)

Which hormone uses phospholipase C as a secondary messenger?
    a. Oxytocin b. Thyroxine c. GH d. ADH
    **Ans: A**

A 45 year old man with a long history of alcoholism presents with severe epigastric pain, nausea, vomiting, fever and increase in serum amylase. Diagnosis of acute pancreatitis superimposed on chronic pancreatitis was made. In this condition, which of the following types of necrosis is most characteristic?
    a. Coagulative necrosis b. Fat necrosis c. Fibrinoid d. Caseous e. Liquefactive necrosis
    **Ans: B**

1) Type of fluid due to appendicitis is:
    a. Exudate b. Transudate c. Serous d. Fibrinous
    **Ans: A**

## Page 6

1) Woman with hyperthyroid features with goiter. Diagnosed with iodine deficiency. Cause of deficiency:
    a. Decreased intake in water and food b. Improper diet c. Defective absorption d. Increased absorption
    **Ans: B**

2) Patient during RTA sustained sacral injury. He presented with overflow incontinence. Where is the lesion?
    a. Sensory nerves b. Parasympathetic c. Sympathetic d. Detrusor muscle e. Spastic
    **Ans: B**

**Explanation:**

- Injury above sacral segment (sympathetic damage): Spastic bladder, automatic bladder, urge incontinence
- Injury at sacral segment (parasympathetic damage): Atonic bladder, autonomous bladder, overflow incontinence

1) A patient is having bleeding problem. Lab shows PT 14 sec, APTT 60 sec (prolonged), bleeding time 6 min. Defect in which pathway?
    a. Extrinsic pathway b. Intrinsic pathway c. Platelet function d. Clot retraction e. Blood propagation
    **Ans: B**

**Explanation:**

- APTT raised only: Hemophilia (intrinsic pathway)
- APTT and BT raised: von Willebrand disease
- All three raised: DIC
- Only BT raised: ITP (low platelets) or platelet function defect
- Heparin monitoring: APTT
- Warfarin monitoring: INR > PT

1) For nutritional assessment of patient, we assess nutrition from his weight loss by:
    a. Trace elements b. Minerals and vitamins c. Albumin and TIBC d. Carbohydrates
    **Ans: C**

2) Muscles of forced expiration:
    a. Quadratus lumborum b. Internal intercostal and Diaphragm c. External intercostal d. Internal intercostal and Rectus abdominis e. Elastic recoil
    **Ans: D**

3) In Christmas disease with increased bleeding, what will be raised?
    a. APTT b. BT c. PT d. Both PT & BT e. Decreased antihemophilic globulin
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- Hemophilia A (classic): decreased factor VIII, APTT raised
- Hemophilia B (Christmas disease): decreased factor IX, APTT raised
- Hemophilia C (Rosenthal syndrome): decreased factor XI

1) With exception of sweat glands, parasympathetic system causes:
    a. Decreased secretions b. Promotes secretions c. Increased HR d. Decreased peristalsis
    **Ans: B**

## Page 7

1) Paraneoplastic syndrome is associated with:
    a. Small cell carcinoma of lung b. Renal cell carcinoma c. Carcinoid d. HCC e. Melanoma
    **Ans: A**

2) On ECG of a girl, you see sawtooth waves, with P waves in a ratio of 3:1. Her pulse is regularly irregular. Which of the following has occurred?
    a. Atrial flutter b. Atrial fibrillation c. Ventricular tachycardia d. Ventricular fibrillation e. Ventricular flutter
    **Ans: A**

3) A surgeon performing thyroidectomy. During upper lobe thyroid surgery, nerve likely to be damaged in proximity with superior thyroid artery is:
    a. Recurrent laryngeal b. External laryngeal nerve c. Internal laryngeal nerve d. Phrenic nerve
    **Ans: C**

**Explanation:**

- Upper lobe: External laryngeal nerve
- Lower lobe: Recurrent laryngeal nerve
- Superior thyroid artery related to: External laryngeal nerve injury
- Inferior thyroid artery related to: Recurrent laryngeal nerve
- Most common nerve injured during thyroidectomy: External laryngeal nerve
- Most common nerve injured during tracheostomy: Recurrent laryngeal nerve
- Hoarseness of voice: Recurrent laryngeal nerve > External laryngeal > Vagus

    **Ans: E**

    a. Hep A b. Hep B c. Hep C d. Hep D e. Hep E
    **Ans: E**

**Explanation:**

- Orofecal route: Hep A > Hep E
- Most lethal hepatitis: Hep D
- Most common in pregnancy: Hep A
- Most lethal/remote area in pregnancy: Hep E

1) A 45 year old previously normal lady started having dyspnea, dry cough, fever 3 months back. Recovered for one month when she went on vacation. Again developed symptoms when she got back to her canaries. X-ray shows multiple nodular lesions in all lung zones. The mechanism of her symptoms was due to:
    a. Antigen-antibody mediated reaction b. Progressive interstitial lung disease c. Mast cell degranulation d. Complement mediated
    **Ans: A** (Hypersensitivity pneumonitis)

2) In crescentic glomerulonephritis, antibody complex deposition on GBM – which type of hypersensitivity?
    a. Type 1 b. Type 2 c. Type 3 d. Type 4
    **Ans: B**

**Explanation:** Overall glomerulonephritis has type 3 HS, but if antibody deposited is mentioned, then type 2 HS.

1) Posteriorly, the inferior limit of lung which we call posterior inferior lobe is at level of:

    **Ans: A**

    a. Closure of semilunar valves b. First heart sound c. Closure of AV valve d. Opening of AV valve

7) Farmer's lung is due to which of the following agents?
    a. Grain dust b. Sugar cane c. Cotton fiber dust d. Coal dust e. Asbestos
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- Grain dust: Farmer's lung
- Aspergillosis: Farmer's lung with granuloma, rhinosinusitis, medial erosion, calcification
- Inorganic dust: Diffuse lung fibrosis on X-ray without fever or cough

1) Hemoglobin begins to appear at which stage?
    a. Early normoblast b. Intermediate normoblast c. Late normoblast d. Reticulocyte
    **Ans: B**

**Explanation:**

- Hemoglobin synthesis starts at early normoblast (prefer proerythroblast if in options)
- In intermediate normoblast, hemoglobin starts to appear
- In late normoblast, nucleus disappears
- Reticulocyte contains highest amount of hemoglobin

## Page 12

1) A patient after RTA having fluent, non-sense speech is due to damage of which area?
    a. Parietal lobe b. Broca area c. Angular gyrus d. Wernicke area e. Frontal lobe
    **Ans: D**

**Explanation:**

- Broca aphasia: motor aphasia, non-fluent, area 44 & 45, inferior frontal gyrus
- Wernicke aphasia: sensory aphasia, fluent non-sense speech, area 22, superior temporal gyrus
- Global aphasia: both, arcuate fasciculus
- Anomic aphasia: mild fluent, failure of word retrieval, angular gyrus

1) Fracture of head of femur leads to avascular necrosis of head. Artery involved is which of following?
    a. Lateral circumflex b. Descending branch lateral circumflex c. Medial circumflex artery d. Femoral artery e. Tibial artery
    **Ans: C**

**Explanation:**

- In adults: Head of femur by retinacular > medial circumflex; Neck of femur by medial and lateral circumflex
- In children: Head of femur by obturator artery

1) Which of the following represents the pressure difference that acts to distend the lungs?
    a. Intrapleural pressure b. Airway opening pressure c. Intrathoracic pressure d. Transpulmonary pressure e. Esophageal pressure

5) In the recovery period after acute inflammation, which factor contributes to decreased repair?
    a. Increased age b. Diabetes mellitus c. Protein deficiencies d. Vitamin C deficiency

    a. 5% b. 10-15% c. 25% d. 50% e. 35%
    **Ans: B**

- Carbs/protein: 4 kcal/g
- Fats: 9 kcal/g
- Alcohol: 7 kcal/g
- Carbs required: 50-60%
- Fats required: 25-35%
- Proteins required: 10-20%

5) A patient presented with Crohn's disease. For treatment of remission, corticosteroids are given. What is best for maintenance of remission of her disease?

    **Ans: C**

- Maintenance of remission: Azathioprine or mercaptopurine (alternative: methotrexate)
- Ulcerative colitis induce remission: aminosalicylates first line, steroids second line
- Maintenance of remission: Azathioprine or mercaptopurine

    a. Sympathetic cholinergic b. Sympathetic adrenergic c. Parasympathetic d. Local metabolites e. Adenosine
    **Ans: A**

4) A woman with 5 weeks of pregnancy contracts German measles. She consults her obstetrician worrying about the baby. Which is the most likely complication the baby might develop?
    a. Aortopulmonary septal defect b. Congenital cataract c. Deafness d. Spina bifida e. Mental retardation
    **Ans: B**

**Explanation:**

- Rubella in pregnancy overall complication: Deafness > Cataract
- Rubella in pregnancy within 5-6 weeks: Heart defect
- Rubella in pregnancy within 7 weeks: Cataract
- Rubella in pregnancy after 7 weeks: Deafness

## Page 17

1) What does PR interval show?
    a. Ventricular repolarization b. SA node conduction to AV node c. SA node conduction to ventricles d. Atrial systole e. Atrial depolarization
    **Ans: C** (PR interval = onset of P wave to onset of QRS – atrial depolarization + AV delay)

2) Atrial stretch leading to tachycardia is:
    a. Hering-Breuer reflex b. Cushing reflex c. Bainbridge reflex d. Sinus tachycardia e. Chemoreceptor
    **Ans: C** (Bainbridge reflex)

3) S1 and S2 heart sounds – the former has:
    a. More frequency b. More duration c. More dullness d. More frequency e. No difference
    **Ans: B** (S1 has longer duration and duller pitch; S2 has higher frequency/pitch)

4) The cause of atherosclerosis is usually:
    a. Endothelial injury b. Hyperlipidemia c. Chronic inflammation d. Infection e. Embolism
    **Ans: A** (Virchow triad: endothelial injury, stasis, hypercoagulability)

5) Nerve compression between C5 and C6 compresses which of following?
    a. C4 b. C5 c. C6 d. C7 e. C3
    **Ans: C** (C6 nerve root exits between C5 and C6)

**Explanation:**

- Cervical roots C1-C7 exit above corresponding vertebrae
- C8 exits below C7
- Thoracic and lumbar roots exit below corresponding vertebrae
- Disc herniation between L4-L5 affects L5 root

    **Ans: B**

2) Antidote for opium is:

    **Ans: C**

3) Intrinsic pathway is activated by which factor?
    a. Factor 2 b. Factor 7 c. Factor 11 d. Factor 10

    a. Knee jerk b. Ankle jerk c. Biceps jerk d. Cremasteric reflex e. Withdrawal reflex
    **Ans: D/E** (Withdrawal reflex is polysynaptic; cremasteric also polysynaptic)

2) A patient diagnosed with atrial fibrillation. How will you manage the patient if he is hemodynamically unstable?
    a. Amiodarone b. Flecainide c. Sotalol d. Lidocaine e. Cardioversion
    **Ans: E** (Electrical cardioversion)

3) What does bacteria secrete which helps in proliferation of new capillaries in wound?
    a. Fibronectin b. Phospholipase c. PDGF d. Metalloproteinase e. FGF
    **Ans: C/E** (PDGF and FGF both promote angiogenesis)

4) A patient has complex partial seizure. How will you treat this patient?
    a. Levetiracetam b. Ethosuximide c. Carbamazepine + Primidone d. Valproate
    **Ans: C** (Carbamazepine is first-line for focal seizures)

5) A patient developed sudden weakness in right upper and lower limbs and mouth deviated to left. Which artery is involved?
    a. ACA b. MCA c. PCA d. Circle of Willis
    **Ans: B** (Middle cerebral artery)

6) Common tumor suppressor gene is:
    a. BRCA b. RET c. P53 d. BCL e. WT1
    **Ans: C**

    a. CCK b. Secretin c. Gastrin d. Somatostatin e. Glucagon
    **Ans: B**

8) 9 months old girl was vaccinated 2 weeks back, now presents with rash all over body, fever. CBC: Hb 13.5g/dl, WBC 6 x 10^9, decreased platelets. Peripheral smear shows large platelets. Diagnosis?
    a. TTP b. ITP c. SLE d. DIC e. Bernard-Soulier syndrome
    **Ans: B** (Post-vaccination ITP – large platelets, low count)

    a. Sartorius b. Gluteus maximus c. Semimembranosus d. Obturator internus
    **Ans: A**

2) A patient with localized circumferential lateral wall infarct. Which artery involved?

- Anterior wall MI (LAD): leads V1-V6
- Lateral wall MI (LCX): leads I, aVL, V5, V6

- Afterload determined by MAP

## Page 26

1) In facial pain, hyperacusis. Ganglion involved is:
    a. Trigeminal ganglion b. Geniculate ganglion c. Ciliary ganglion d. Pterygopalatine ganglion
    **Ans: B** (Geniculate neuralgia)
