    **Ans: A**

3) Lipid bilayer of cell membrane has cholesterol in its structure. Function of this cholesterol in membrane is:
    a. Intercellular attachment b. Permits ion movement c. Solubility d. Phagocytosis
    **Ans: B** (Maintains membrane fluidity and permeability)

4) Hyperexcitability of neuron due to deficiency of which of the following in ECF?
    a. Na b. Mg c. Ca d. K e. Cl
    **Ans: C** (Hypocalcemia → increased neuronal excitability)

**Explanation:** Ca guards Na channels on neuronal membrane. Less Ca → less guarding → more Na influx → hyperexcitability.

## Page 32

1) Middle meningeal artery is a branch of:
    a. Cerebral artery b. Mandibular artery c. Occipital artery d. Temporal artery e. Maxillary artery
    **Ans: E**

    a. GLUT 1 b. GLUT 2 c. GLUT 4 d. Facilitated diffusion e. Active transport
    **Ans: C**

3) Insulin-independent glucose uptake occurs in:
    a. Hypothalamus b. Myocardium c. Resting skeletal muscles d. Exercising skeletal muscles e. Liver
    **Ans: D** (Exercise increases GLUT4 translocation independently of insulin)

4) Which of the following interleukins will cause increase of red blood cells from T lymphocytes?
    a. IL-2 b. IL-3 c. IL-6 d. IL-8 e. IL-4
    **Ans: B** (IL-3 stimulates multilineage hematopoiesis)

5) A man during road traffic accident got injury to cervical sympathetic chain. Most likely change in eye is:
    a. Ipsilateral drooping of eyelids b. Ipsilateral mydriasis c. Flushing of face on opposite side d. Sweating on ipsilateral side e. Ciliary muscle paralysis
    **Ans: A** (Horner syndrome – ptosis)

6) A young female had RTA which resulted in femur fracture for which she had prosthesis placed. She developed SOB and petechiae the same day. Most probable cause:
    a. Fat embolism b. Pulmonary embolism c. Air embolism d. Amniotic fluid embolism e. Sepsis
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- Air embolism: history of CVP line then SOB
- Pregnant + long bone fracture + death within 24h or during labour: amniotic fluid embolism
- Sudden death + sudden SOB: pulmonary embolism
- Long bone fracture: death after 3-5 days → fat embolism

1) Anterior pituitary removal leads to:
    a. Short stature b. Absence of menses c. Short width d. Excessive menses
    **Ans: B** (Loss of FSH/LH → amenorrhea)

    **Ans: E**

## Page 34

1) A lady with CRF had her blood sample taken which was placed in refrigerator overnight. Next day: normal Na, raised K 6.3, raised PO4 and LDH 600. What is the cause?
    a. End stage renal failure b. Hemolysis of blood sample c. Hemolysis of tissue d. Renal CA e. Drug intoxication
    **Ans: B**

2) 42-year-old para 3 reported heavy cyclic menstrual bleeding for last 6 months. Clinical examination unremarkable. Recent D&C histopathology showed early secretory phase endometrium. First line treatment?
    a. Antifibrinolytic agent b. GnRH analogues c. Mefenamic acid d. Danazol
    **Ans: C** (Dysfunctional uterine bleeding – NSAID first line)

3) Cohort in Epidemiology is defined as:
    a. Study of population in a city b. Study of country c. Study of a case or sample d. Incidence rate e. Used to describe variability
    **Ans: C**

    a. Sepsis b. DIC c. Decreased factor 8 d. Hypovolemic shock

    a. Prostacyclin b. Thromboxane A2 c. COX 2 synthesis d. COX 3 e. Platelet formation

## Page 35

1) Decreased lymphatic flow due to:
    a. Decreased arterial pressure b. Hemorrhage c. Increased hydrostatic pressure d. Increased permeability e. Exercise
    **Ans: B**

**Explanation:**

- Increased lymphatic flow: increased hydrostatic pressure, decreased oncotic pressure
- Decreased lymphatic flow: decreased hydrostatic pressure, increased oncotic pressure, hemorrhage

1) Lady has difficulty coming down stairs and tilts head to left with eye upward while moving downstairs. Lesion is at?
    a. Oculomotor nerve b. Trochlear nerve c. Abducens nerve d. Trigeminal nerve
    **Ans: B** (CN IV – superior oblique; tilts head away from affected side)

2) Most significant cause of atheroma:
    a. Immobilization b. Diastolic hypertension c. Type 2 personality d. Endothelial injury e. Diabetes
    **Ans: B** (Hypertension is major risk factor)

3) Calculate GFR when: Glomerular hydrostatic pressure = 60 mmHg, Bowman capsule hydrostatic pressure = 12 mmHg, capillary oncotic pressure = 30 mmHg.
    a. 18 b. 84 c. 92 d. 112 e. 48
    **Ans: A** (GFR = (PGC - PBC) - (πGC - πBC) = (60-30) - (12-0) = 30-12 = 18)

4) A hypertensive patient can be managed pharmacologically and surgically. On labs, what evidence makes it possible for him to be treated pharmacologically instead of surgery?
    a. Increased catecholamines b. Hyperreninemia c. Hyperaldosteronism d. Hypercalcemia e. Inflammatory response to kidney
    **Ans: B** (Renal artery stenosis – surgery; essential HTN – medication)

5) In ECG, heart rate is 120/min. It is related to:
    a. R-R interval will be 0.5 sec b. QRS complex will be less than 0.02 sec c. T wave will be greater than 2 mV d. R-R interval will be 1 sec
    **Ans: A** (60/120 = 0.5 sec)

6) A group of mice was taken and injection of plastic hydrocarbon was given. This will work as initiator. The initiator will work as:
    a. Slow process will take time b. Permanent DNA damage c. It is last step in carcinogenesis d. Causes clonal proliferation
    **Ans: B**

7) A mother brought her few months old baby. Child is case of meningitis. She is worried that her two elder children might get the infection. What is the mode of infection?
    a. Respiratory droplets b. Blood c. Blood transfusion d. Sexual contact e. Needle stick injury
    **Ans: A**

1) Sacral hiatus is formed by:

2) Athletes have enlarged heart size and increased stroke volume, yet their muscles need same amount of energy and cardiac output is approximately same as normal. Reason for this phenomenon?
    a. Increased SV b. Increased SV and heart rate c. Decreased heart rate and increased SV d. Increased TPR e. Increased venous return and increased HR

- Capsule: interlobular artery

- Hilum: segmental artery

1) A young girl has history of SOB and wheezing. Investigations reveal C1 deficiency and she lacks an esterase required by the body. Most likely diagnosis:

## Page 39

1) Which of the following is released early in stress?
    a. CRH b. TSH c. ACTH d. Cortisol e. Epinephrine
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- Early in stress: CRH > ACTH > Cortisol
- Stress hormone: Cortisol > ACTH
- Stress + vasoconstriction: Epinephrine

1) Which metabolite of Vitamin D is used for laboratory assessment?

5) Athlete playing high jump now presented with pain in gluteal region. On examination, cannot flex hip and extend knee at same time. Damage to which of the following?

8) Patient on ATT with big toe swelling. Most likely due to:

- Isoniazid: peripheral neuropathy
- Rifampicin: red/orange urine
- Ethambutol: optic neuritis
- Pyrazinamide: hyperuricemia (gout)

## Page 42

1) Student examining a slide visualizes a tumor of muscle of GIT. A protein which connects cells together is missing. The protein is:

2) Carbonic anhydrase is very useful as it catalyzes conversion of CO2 to bicarbonate. It is located in:
    a. Cytoplasm of neutrophil b. Cytoplasm of basophil c. Cell membrane of RBC d. Cytoplasm of RBC e. Cell membrane of neutrophil
    **Ans: D**

3) Increased ECF potassium – what will be the effect on heart?
    a. Myocardial weakness b. Spastic paralysis c. Diastolic cardiac arrest d. Systolic cardiac arrest e. Tremors
    **Ans: C**

**Explanation:**

- Hypercalcemia & hypokalemia: systolic heart arrest
- Hypocalcemia & hyperkalemia: diastolic heart arrest

1) Localized edema is formed by accumulation of lymph due to lymphatic obstruction. Which supports the above statement?
    a. Inflammation and fibrosis b. Increased hydrostatic pressure c. Decreased oncotic pressure d. Renal failure and hypoproteinemia e. Heart failure
    **Ans: A**

2) A person wants to identify acid-fast bacilli. Which feature is unique to acid-fast bacilli?
    a. Cell wall made of peptidoglycan b. Capsule c. Mycolic acids d. Periplasmic space

3) A pregnant lady with 5 weeks of gestational amenorrhea presented to OPD. She was diagnosed with German measles. Which complication is the fetus most likely to have?
    a. B/L cataract b. Deafness c. Aortopulmonary heart defect d. Conjunctivitis e. Mental retardation
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- Rubella in pregnancy overall: deafness > cataract
- Within 7 weeks: cataract
- After 7 weeks: deafness

## Page 43

1) Which of the following is a measure of dispersion?
    a. Standard deviation b. Mean c. Median d. Mode
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- Measures of central tendency: mean, median, mode
- Measures of dispersion: standard deviation, range, variance

1) Which of the following produces maximum vasoconstriction?
    a. Bupivacaine b. Cocaine c. Procaine d. Rocuronium e. Prilocaine
    **Ans: B** (Cocaine has potent vasoconstrictor effect)

2) Negatively charged particles are prevented from entering renal basement membrane. Which component is responsible for prevention?
    a. Proteoglycan b. Laminin c. Densely packed cells d. Lamina of lamina interna e. Fibronectin
    **Ans: A**

3) GBM repels proteins due to negative charge due to which of the following?
    a. Proteoglycan b. Collagen type IV c. Fibronectin d. Endothelium e. Laminin
    **Ans: A** (Heparan sulfate proteoglycans)

4) Common to glucagon and epinephrine is:
    a. Glycogenesis b. Glycogenolysis in liver & skeletal muscle c. Activate insulin d. Cause hypoglycemia e. Reactivate phosphoryl kinase in liver
    **Ans: B**

5) Glucagon increases due to:
    a. Exercise b. High glucose c. Epinephrine d. Somatostatin e. Starvation
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- Increase glucagon: hypoglycemia, arginine, CCK, NE, epinephrine, ACh, exercise
- Decrease glucagon: hyperglycemia, insulin, somatostatin, fatty acids, ketoacids

1) Ureteric bud not reaching metanephric mesenchyme will lead to:
    a. Ureter without kidney b. Polycystic kidney c. Renal agenesis d. Kidney without ureter e. Pelvic kidney
    **Ans: A** (Ureteric bud induces metanephros; if fails, kidney doesn't form; ureter may be present but non-functional)

2) Genotype of true hermaphrodite is:

    **Ans: A** (Most common 46,XX; but true hermaphrodite can be XX, XY, or mosaic; options limited)

    a. Pleomorphism b. N/C ratio c. Invasion of surrounding tissues d. Infarction

## Page 47 (continued)

1) In a patient with cirrhosis presenting with acquired bleeding abnormalities, which lab finding is most consistent?
    a. Prolonged bleeding time b. Prolonged prothrombin time c. Prolonged aPTT d. Decreased albumin e. Normal clotting time
    **Ans: B** (Vitamin K deficiency → prolonged PT)

2) A dancer moves smoothly and rhythmically in sync with music. Which function of the motor cortex is primarily responsible?
    a. Integration of sensory information b. Planning and execution of movement c. Coordination of balance d. Maintenance of muscle tone e. Regulation of reflexes
    **Ans: B**

3) A patient presented with megaloblastic anemia. On investigation, there is orotic acid in urine, leading to increased synthesis of which?
    a. Purine b. Pyrimidine c. Sphingomyelin d. Cholesterol e. Glycogen
    **Ans: B** (Orotic aciduria – pyrimidine synthesis defect)

4) Bond between actin covered by tropomyosin is between:
    a. Actin-tropomyosin b. Troponin I - troponin C c. Actin - I band d. Actin-myosin e. Actin-troponin
    **Ans: E**

5) 43 year old lady with 3 children and normal reproductive cycle has less chance of pregnancy compared to 3.7 year old female. Reason?
    a. Uterine tumor b. Low LH surge c. Inhibition of GnRH d. GnRH becomes desensitized after menopause
    **Ans: C** (Age-related decline in fertility)

6) Which of the following is true about plasma proteins?
    a. Exert oncotic pressure of 25 mmHg b. Globulins make up the bulk c. Made exclusively in liver d. Buffer capacity up to 30%
    **Ans: A**

## Page 48 (Medicine 21 August Morning – excerpt)

*[This section contains a new exam session. Key points:]*

1) After half of liver transplant, remaining half regenerates in?
    a. 2 weeks b. 6 weeks c. 5 to 15 days d. 16 to 25 days e. 100 to 150 days
    **Ans: C**

2) Cell repolarization occurs due to outward movement of:
    a. Sodium b. Potassium c. Chloride d. Magnesium
    **Ans: B**

3) 16-year-old with 15 year history of diabetes. How to check long-term glycemic control?
    a. Fasting blood sugar b. Glycosylated hemoglobin c. Insulin level d. Glucagon level
    **Ans: B**

4) Which is connective tissue in brain?
    a. Parietal cells b. Chief cells c. Paneth cells d. Oligodendrocytes e. Basal cells
    **Ans: D**

5) Pars nervosa supporting cells:
    a. Oligodendrocytes b. Pituicytes c. Kupffer cells d. Astrocytes
    **Ans: B**

6) 16 weeks pregnant lady with ultrasound finding of increased amniotic fluid. Advised beta-HCG and later AFP. AFP raised. Likely diagnosis?
    a. Spina bifida occulta b. Renal agenesis c. Down syndrome d. Anencephaly e. Dextrocardia
    **Ans: D** (Open neural tube defect → high AFP)

7) Crista galli is extension of which bone?
    a. Sphenoid b. Zygomatic c. Ethmoid d. Maxilla
    **Ans: C**

8) Sella turcica is part of which bone?
    a. Sphenoid b. Zygomatic c. Ethmoid d. Nasal
    **Ans: A**

9) The H+/K+ pump in parietal cells is controlled by:
    a. Carbonic anhydrase b. Na+/K+ ATPase c. Renin d. K+/H+ ATPase e. Cyclooxygenase
    **Ans: D**

10) Patient with palpitations, absent P waves, irregular pulse, irregular R-R interval, and diastolic rumbling murmur. Likely cause?
    a. Mitral stenosis with insufficiency b. Aortic stenosis c. Pulmonic stenosis d. Aortic regurgitation
    **Ans: A** (Atrial fibrillation + mitral stenosis)

11) Which ATT drug causes orange-colored urine?
    a. INH b. Rifampicin c. Streptomycin d. Pyrazinamide
    **Ans: B**

12) Patient on peritoneal dialysis. Plasma K+ 6.5. What to advise him to avoid?
    a. Cereals b. Yogurt c. Apple d. Tomatoes e. Carrots
    **Ans: E** (Carrots are high in potassium; tomatoes also high, but carrots often listed)

## Page 49

1) During a fight, person is stabbed in the stomach bed. Which artery is damaged?
    a. SMA b. Hepatic artery c. IMA d. Splenic artery
    **Ans: D** (Stomach bed – splenic artery)

2) Neostriatum contains:
    a. Caudate + putamen b. Caudate + lentiform c. Caudate + globus pallidus externa d. Caudate + globus pallidus interna e. Globus pallidus externa + lentiform
    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- Neostriatum: caudate + putamen
- Corpus striatum: caudate + lentiform
- Paleostriatum: globus pallidus
- Lentiform nucleus: globus pallidus + putamen

1) After vasectomy, seminal fluid will contain:
    a. Seminal and prostatic fluid b. Prostatic fluid only c. Sperm count decreased d. Prostatic fluid and sperm only
    **Ans: A** (No sperm, but seminal vesicle and prostatic secretions remain)

2) Patient with vomiting and signs of dehydration. Urea 70, Cr 0.8. Cause?
    a. Post-renal azotemia b. Pre-renal azotemia c. ATN d. CKD e. Glomerulonephritis
    **Ans: B** (High BUN/Cr ratio >20 suggests pre-renal)

3) After trauma, all muscles of abdomen and chest paralyzed but still breathing. Level of injury?
    a. C4 b. Below C5 c. T4 d. T12
    **Ans: B** (Diaphragm intact – C3-5; intercostals and abdominals lost → below C5)

4) After trauma, injury to ilioinguinal nerve. What will be the deficit?
    a. Lateral thigh sensation lost b. Loss of dorsiflexion c. Cremasteric reflex and medial thigh sensation lost d. Loss of testicular reflex and lateral thigh sensation
    **Ans: C**

5) Shortest half-life is of:
    a. GnRH b. Aldosterone c. Testosterone d. Prolactin
    **Ans: A** (GnRH half-life ~2-4 minutes)

6) 55-year-old female taking phenothiazine was observed to have slow, writhing movement in an attempt to remove a fly resting on her nose. This is mostly likely due to:
    a. Parkinsonism b. Athetosis c. Ballismus d. Hemiballismus
    **Ans: B** (Tardive dyskinesia – athetoid movements)

    **Ans: D**

- Motion sickness: scopolamine > meclizine
- Mountain sickness: acetazolamide
- Air sickness: meclozine > cyclizine

1) Patient with severe headache, vomiting, neck stiffness, raised ICP. LP showed blood-stained CSF. Diagnosis?
    a. Subdural hemorrhage b. Cerebral hemorrhage c. Extradural hematoma d. Subarachnoid hemorrhage e. Intraparenchymal hemorrhage
    **Ans: D**

2) Patient with polyuria, polydipsia, urine osmolality 310 mOsm, known multiple myeloma. Cause of polyuria?
    a. Renal tubules do not respond to ADH b. Psychogenic polydipsia c. Decreased ADH d. Increased aldosterone
    **Ans: A** (Nephrogenic DI due to myeloma)

3) Patient with decreased neutrophils, increased lymphocytes, increased eosinophils, increased ACTH. Likely diagnosis?
    a. Cushing syndrome b. Cushing disease c. Ectopic ACTH d. Leukemia e. Addison's disease
    **Ans: E**

**Explanation:**

- Addison's: low cortisol → high ACTH → low neutrophils, high lymphocytes, high eosinophils
- Cushing: high cortisol → low ACTH → high neutrophils, low lymphocytes, low eosinophils

1) True regarding heart muscle:

    a. Epinephrine b. Norepinephrine c. Dopamine and dobutamine d. Atropine
    **Ans: C**

**Explanation:**

- Cardiogenic shock: dopamine & dobutamine
- Anaphylactic shock: adrenaline
- Septic shock: norepinephrine

- Bradycardia: atropine

## Page 60

    a. Rapid inflow b. Atrial contraction c. Slow ejection d. Isovolumetric relaxation
    **Ans: A**

- S1: isovolumetric contraction (closure of AV valves)
- S2: isovolumetric relaxation (closure of semilunar valves)
- S3: rapid ventricular filling
- S4: atrial systole

2) Man inhaling silica dust for 6 years, developed cough. 1 cm mass on X-ray. Cells seen in lungs?
    a. Foreign body giant cells b. Eosinophils c. Lymphocytes d. Silicosis
    **Ans: A** (Silicotic nodule – giant cells)

3) Patient after RTA resuscitated. Earliest sign of successful resuscitation:
    a. Decreased heart rate b. Increased urine output c. Decreased urine output d. Increased BP
    **Ans: B**

4) Patient with ataxia with both eyes open and closed. Lesion in:
    a. Cerebellum b. Cerebellar peduncle c. DCML tract d. Left internal capsule e. Cortex
    **Ans: A** (Romberg's sign: falls with eyes closed only = DCML; falls with both = cerebellum)

5) Person went to 3rd floor via stairs, increased cardiac output. Cause?
    a. Increased preload b. Decreased contractility c. Decreased sympathetic d. Increased TPR
    **Ans: A** (Increased venous return)

6) Female with hyperprolactinemia diagnosed with pituitary adenoma. Tumor growth anteriorly will compress?
    a. Cavernous sinus b. Optic nerve c. Optic chiasm d. Optic tract e. Trochlear nerve
    **Ans: B** (Anteriorly – optic nerve)

**Explanation:**

- Laterally: cavernous sinus
- Inferiorly: sphenoid sinus
- Superiorly: optic chiasm
- Anteriorly: optic nerve

## Page 63

1) Patient with retrosternal chest pain, nausea, GERD, velvety esophagus with columnar epithelium. Increased risk of?
    a. Esophagitis b. Barrett esophagus c. Mallory-Weiss tear d. Gastritis
    **Ans: B**

2) Man working in factory has neuronal degeneration due to exposure to:
    a. Organophosphate poisoning b. Arsenic poisoning c. Lead poisoning d. Aspirin poisoning
    **Ans: C** (Lead – peripheral neuropathy)

3) Person with history of smoking and drinking, endoscopy shows mass in middle third of esophagus. Likely?
    a. Adenocarcinoma b. Squamous cell carcinoma c. Barrett esophagus d. Chronic esophagitis e. Gastritis
    **Ans: B**

**Explanation:**

- Upper/middle 2/3: squamous cell carcinoma (alcohol, smoking, achalasia)
- Lower 1/3: adenocarcinoma (GERD, Barrett, obesity)

    **Ans: A**

**Explanation:**

- CN V motor: jaw deviates toward lesion
- CN X: uvula deviates away from lesion
- CN XI: weakness turning head contralateral, shoulder droop
- CN XII: tongue deviates toward lesion

## Page 68 (Medicine 22 August Afternoon – start)

    **Ans: C**

    a. IgM b. IgG1 c. IgG4 d. IgM e. IgA
    **Ans: B** (Maternal IgG crosses placenta)

    a. TB b. Cat scratch disease c. Leprosy d. Sarcoidosis
    **Ans: D** (Sarcoidosis – non-caseating; AFB positive? Possibly atypical; but sarcoid can have false-positive AFB? More likely TB if AFB+; but question says non-caseating – sarcoid)

    a. Angiotensin II b. Renin c. ADH d. Cortisol e. ACTH
    **Ans: B**

**Explanation:**

- Primary hyperaldosteronism: high aldosterone, low renin
- Secondary hyperaldosteronism: high aldosterone, high renin
